EP: DENAI MOORE - THE LAKE|<div style="text-align: justify;">19 year old <b>Denai Moore</b> was born in Jamaica but grew up in Stratford, East London. She's apparently been making music since she was 7 years old, and has already toured alongside <i>Tom Odell</i>, appeared on the <i>Jools Holland</i> show, and her recently released debut EP titled '<b>The Lake</b>' was produced by <i>Ben Drew</i>. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The first song on the EP is the title track '<b>The Lake</b>'. It's instantly powerful, with a sombre piano and distant guitar playing whilst Denai demonstrates her wonderfully talented vocals. Her voice almost sounds like its being held back whilst the listener gets sucked in by the melodies, it's like a musical trojan horse.<br/><br/>'<b>Everything</b>' starts off on in a similar vein, with the music being quite stripped back, very much like the approach on the first <i>James Blake </i>record. However things take an unexpected uptake in beat halfway through, with Denai expressing a more positive tone and a fair amount of groove.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>Part 2</b>' is the final track on the record, it's a delicate love song flowing from positive to negative and back again, and is sure to thaw the most frozen of hearts and minds. During the course of the EP there's nods towards the likes of <i>Speech Debelle</i>, <i>Feist</i>, the aforementioned <i>James Blake</i>,<i> Cat Power</i> even, but the over-riding thought is of how Denai has her own carefully crafted sound which is built around folk but is heavily influenced by soul.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Whilst her vocal delivery and approach is a clear stand out feature on this EP, there is also a prominence in her song writing ability, with a clear appreciation of timings and space within her songs. 'The Lake' is a brief snapshot of what this talented young woman is capable of and we're certain interested to follow her progress over the time to come. // <a href="http://www.denaimoore.com/" target="_blank"><b>Denai Moore</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div>||
THE UK BLOG SOUND OF 2014|<div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Music Liberation</b> is once again both pleased and privileged to have taken part in this years <b>UK Blog Sound </b>poll.<br/><br/>This year we are excited to reveal that two of our three chosen artists have made the final list of 16 - <b>Sophie Jamieson</b> and <b>Mt. Wolf</b>.<br/><br/>There are also two acts who we nominated last time out who have made this years one - <b>Marika Hackman</b> and <b>Wolf Alice</b>. Not that we like to blow our own trumpets or anything!</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">For those of you unaware here's some background on the Blog Sound poll:-</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The Blog Sound Poll was first published in 2011. The concept of the poll wasn’t to criticise the established BBC Sound of list, but simply an experiment to see if UK music bloggers could come up with its own list of emerging artists that was more representative of their community and give the artists that were nominated some extra publicity. Indeed the idea was to compliment the BBC list in many ways by providing an alternative to compare and contrast.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The 2011 list contained some interesting alternatives to the BBC list including Mercury Prize winners Alt-J and Bastille who have found huge commercial success in the UK in 2013. The 2012 list was more similar to the BBC list with Haim being the runaway winners, followed closely by Chvrches.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The UK Blog Sound of 2014 poll is the biggest yet with 59 blogs each nominating their 3 favourite emerging artists. It has been retitled to give emphasis to the fact that it is a list created by UK bloggers, although the choices of music can come from around the world. This year however, 14 of the 16 most voted for artists are British.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The winning act and close runners up will be revealed on the 2nd of January in a short list of three.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">This list contains a range of artists that have all received strong coverage from UK bloggers over the last year and can therefore be seen to be a good representation of what music bloggers have been enjoying listening to.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The music blogs that took part in the voting were:-</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="ecxMsoNormal" EP: KID KARATE - LIGHTS OUT|<div style="text-align: justify;">Vocalist and guitarist <i>Kevin Breen</i> and drummer <i>Steven Gannon</i> make up <b>Kid Karate</b>, a duo from Dublin who earlier this year released their EP '<b>Lights Out</b>'. Get prepared for big riffs, big drums, big vocals, basically it's just a big slice of rock pie. BIG.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">To start let's mention some similar sounding bands to Kid Karate, such as, and in no particular order, - <i>Black Keys</i>, <i>DZ Deathrays</i>, <i>Middle Class Rut</i>, <i>Jack White</i>, <i>Fugazi</i>...I could go on, but I think you'll get the picture. This is loud, unashamedly brash rock music that is built upon monster riffs and driven forward by Gannon's tribal drumming, amongst which all the while your brain gets melted by Kevin Breen's manic vocals. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>Two Times</b>', the lead track from the record, is a perfect introduction to the band. You'll be sure to have lyrics such as '<i>I ain't comin' back, you won't hear from me no more!</i>' seared into your brain after just one listen. The music may sound simple yet it's this raw element that makes it so exciting, good rock music should be like this, letting the listener in easily before holding onto them for dear life kicking and screaming!</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Other tracks on the EP include the slow burning '<b>Heart</b>', and the groovy as fuck '<b>This City</b>'. The record closes with '<b>You Need Violence</b>', which is perhaps the most different sounding track on the album, featuring a higher tempo and a relentless drive to punish the listener throughout. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>Lights Out</b>' is one of the most exhilarating EP's we've come across this year, a record that has a singular desire from <b>Kid Karate</b> to utilise raw passion and determination to celebrate all that is great with rock music. *Much recommended for you rock heads out there! // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/kidkaratemusic" target="_blank"><b>Kid Karate</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div>||
EP: VANCE JOY - GOD ONLY LOVES YOU WHEN YOU'RE DANCING|<div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Vance Joy</b> is an Australian singer songwriter from Melbourne, who later this month releases his latest body of work, an EP titled '<b>God Only Loves You When You're Dancing</b>' which is coming out through <b>Infectious Music</b> on November 25th. He visited the UK for a mini tour last month and will return again before the end of the year with a one-off show at St Stephens Church on December 4th.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Having already had airplay on Radio 1 and a critically acclaimed performance at this years SXSW, not to mention the proposed recording of an album for Atlantic next year, it's fair to say this EP is a fair reflection of where Vance Joy is at, as well as where he is going in the future.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>Emmylou</b>' is the first track on the EP, a beautiful introduction to the vocal prowess that Joy commands, his voice sounds believable, a striking combination of fragility and confidence. The track builds slowly at first with just a guitar, but gradually more elements are added almost seamlessly before we've almost entered pop territory without even noticing it. '<b>Riptide</b>' is the single of the record, clearly taking reference from folk such as the Lumineers with big heartfelt vocals which are hard to not get taken in by. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>Play With Fire</b>' carries on in a similar vain, but it is '<b>Snaggletooth</b>' where we discover a different dimension to the record. Here emphasis is again placed upon both the vocal delivery and lyrics, as well as some gorgeous strings which give the song extra oomph. There's some guitar finger picking action half way through which breaks things up, but it is the appreciation of space within the song which sets it apart from others on the EP and suggests at greater depth possible on a longer record. The album finishes with '<b>From Afar</b>', a romantic song that will touch the majority of us and is a lovely way to finish the EP.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Comparisons with <b>Vance Joy</b> can be drawn with the likes of singer songwriters such as <i>Benjamin Francis Leftwich</i> and <i>Keaton Henson</i>, but you can also pick out the likes of <i>The Lumineers</i> and <i>The National</i> within his work, meaning '<b>God Only Loves You When You're Dancing</b>' is a record that should please many and his is a name we should look out for in the year to come. // <a href="http://vancejoy.com/" target="_blank"><b>Vance Joy</b></a> // <a href="http://www.infectiousmusicuk.com/" target="_blank"><b>Infectious Music</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div>||
NEW MUSIC: DRENGE|<div style="text-align: justify;">One of the more exciting bands to emerge in recent times are <b>Drenge</b>, a sibling duo from Sheffield (Rory and Eoin Loveless), who recently released their debut self titled album on <b>Infectious Music</b>. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Combining grunge and garage rock there is a real swagger to their music which oozes self confidence, and is pure heaven for those of us who are head bangers / foot tappers. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Be sure to check them out live when they are supporting Peace on their UK tour in December! / <a href="http://www.drenge,co.uk/" target="_blank"><b>Drenge</b></a> // <a href="http://www.infectiousmusicuk.com/" target="_blank"><b>Infectious Music</b></a></div>||
INTERVIEW: MACKENZIE SCOTT (TORRES)|<div style="text-align: justify;">Back in February of this year we <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/2013/02/album-torres-torres.html" target="_blank">reviewed</a> the self titled debut album from <b>Torres</b> aka <b>Mackenzie Scott</b>, a 22 year old from Nashville, Tennessee, who wowed us with her record which we described as '<i>bold, authentic, and full of integrity</i>'.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">It's fair to say the record is still one of our favourites of the year, and should feature high in our end of year lists. Ahead of the album's UK/European release on the 11th of November and supporting European tour, we were lucky enough to track her down for a few words.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>- First off I’d like to thank you for taking time out to talk to us here at Music Liberation, and for making one of our favourite albums so far this year!</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>- For those who may not know you here in the UK yet, how would you describe your music?</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"<i>Dark songs about life and the human condition, both of which are also dark</i>."</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; text-align: right;"><tbody><tr><td style="text-align: center;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-EO2nTVR0KYs/UlMNpor9oCI/AAAAAAAAE08/WW6LxFB20rA/s1600/995750_216199318532123_760499425_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-EO2nTVR0KYs/UlMNpor9oCI/AAAAAAAAE08/WW6LxFB20rA/s320/995750_216199318532123_760499425_n.jpg" width="320"/></a></td></tr><tr><td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;">Photo by Nuria Rius</td></tr></tbody></table><b><span id="goog_2007340088"></span><span id="goog_2007340089"></span>- Where do you get your inspiration from?</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"<i>Mostly, I'm inspired by Detective Olivia Benson from Law and Order: SVU. Almost anything inspires me. I watched a mother put Chapstick on her sleeping son's lips while riding the subway the other day and was inspired.</i>"</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>- Your debut album receives its UK/European release in November, excited much?</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"<i>MUCH excitement.</i>"</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>- You have a UK/European tour supporting the release, have you played over here much before?</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"<i>I've only played the UK thus far, namely London and Manchester. I still have so much European ground to cover.</i>"</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>- How did your last London show go?</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"<i>It was one of the most fun shows I've ever played.</i>"</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>- You have a couple of London shows, one supporting Daughter, do you know much about them?</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"<i>I am familiar with Daughter and I'm really looking forward to meeting those folks.</i>"</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-zKr8i36AyDg/UlMOcV46SxI/AAAAAAAAE1I/wxUB6yfWXCw/s1600/1010972_10153271539960431_2046834646_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="265" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-zKr8i36AyDg/UlMOcV46SxI/AAAAAAAAE1I/wxUB6yfWXCw/s400/1010972_10153271539960431_2046834646_n.jpg" width="400"/></a></div><b>- What are your tour essentials?</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"<i>Emergen-C packets, a sleeping bag, probiotics, Tums, and black pants.</i>"</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>- What can we expect from a Torres live show?</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"<i>Things get a little messier and louder than you'd expect. The rawness that falls through the cracks on the record is revealed with the live show. If I bring a band with me, you'll probably want ear plugs.</i>"</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>- We’d love to pick up a 12” of your record at the London show, any chance you’ll have them with you?!</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"<i>I will. I'd love for you to have one!</i>"</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">-<i>Mackenzie</i></div><div style="text-align: justify;">  </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>A big thank you to Mackenzie for her time, we look forward to saying hello at the London Borderline show on the 13th, and checking out that live show. // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/TORRESMUSICOFFICIAL" target="_blank">Torres</a></b><br/><br/><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="https://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F73488813" width="100%"></iframe></div>||
SINGLE: FOSSIL COLLECTIVE - THE WATER|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-R2CQ0Af9Uwg/UkQxUFb_iWI/AAAAAAAAEz8/CsoKvgMKUhk/s1600/fossil+collective.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-R2CQ0Af9Uwg/UkQxUFb_iWI/AAAAAAAAEz8/CsoKvgMKUhk/s320/fossil+collective.jpg" width="320"/></a></div></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/><b>Fossil Collective</b> are a duo from Leeds (<i>Jonny Hooker</i> and <i>David Fendick</i>), who release their new EP '<b>The Water</b>' on October 28th through <b>Dirty Hit</b>.<br/><br/>Check out the gorgeous lead and title track below...<br/><br/></div>||
NEW MUSIC: JETPLANE LANDING - DON'T TRY|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-7RXkNQzB_9E/UiywEeIIaGI/AAAAAAAAEzs/z4p1jSb_nFo/s1600/3810756707df84482c3e803b1f8546d1cea44776.jpg.pagespeed.ce.1dvxXCZzvs.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-7RXkNQzB_9E/UiywEeIIaGI/AAAAAAAAEzs/z4p1jSb_nFo/s1600/3810756707df84482c3e803b1f8546d1cea44776.jpg.pagespeed.ce.1dvxXCZzvs.jpg"/></a></div>Irish post hardcore rockers <b>Jetplane Landing</b> return this year with their fourth album '<b>Don't Try</b>', their first record since 2007's '<b>Backlash Cop</b>'.<br/><br/>The new album is a visceral delight, clocking in at under 40 minutes, the 4-piece from Derry in Northern Ireland draw upon various hard rock genres to produce a solid body of work that does more than a little to cement their place amongst contemporaries such as <i>Biffy Clyro</i>,<i> Les Savy Fav</i>, and even more legendary bands such as <i>Refused</i> and <i>At The Drive-In</i>.<br/><br/>The music put forward is positive, with guitar riffs aplenty and the vocals also celebratory in nature, with the opening single '<b>My Radio Heart</b>' a perfect example of this. The band are on tour throughout September in support of the new album.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Don't Try is available now through <a href="http://www.smalltownamerica.co.uk/" target="_blank"><b>Smalltown America</b></a> - <b><a href="http://www.smalltownamerica.co.uk/"></a></b> // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/JetplaneLanding?fref=ts" target="_blank"><b>Jetplane Landing</b></a></div>||
SINGLE: LOS PORCOS - SUNSHINE / C.F.W|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-m1F727IrzVg/UhN88J6EL_I/AAAAAAAAAAY/PGdwYdmYtxk/s1600/71798_418192218266755_8847281_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="240" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-m1F727IrzVg/UhN88J6EL_I/AAAAAAAAAAY/PGdwYdmYtxk/s320/71798_418192218266755_8847281_n.jpg" width="320"/></a></div><b>Los Porcos</b> is the new summery nu-disco indie infused musical incarnation of former indie rock music makers <i>Wu Lyf</i>, who, always evasive of press attention, saw a massive transformation following frontman <i>Ellery James Roberts</i>’ surprise departure at the end of 2012.  Now similarly elusive 7-piece Los Porcos are set to release their double A-side “<b>Sunshine/C.F.W</b>.” this September 15 on <b>Caledonia Records</b>.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">With its indie dance beats and 70s guitar jangles, chunky wah wah guitar riffs and light-up dance-floor funk flashbacks: opening track “<b>Sunshine</b>” is a feel-good pop-rocked tune with a catchy chorus of rippling vocals and a heavy sprinkling of classic disco. Meanwhile on the flipside ‘<b>C.F.W.</b>’ (<i>Classically Feminine Woman</i>) with similarly vintage disco funk infused feel, is a smooth, laid back dance pop track underpinned by sunny beats, tastefully vocoded vocals and jangling upbeat funk guitar.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-V0FFDzxnNPM/UhN9ZHMaVGI/AAAAAAAAAAg/vyirECZjeMs/s1600/image001.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="209" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-V0FFDzxnNPM/UhN9ZHMaVGI/AAAAAAAAAAg/vyirECZjeMs/s320/image001.jpg" width="320"/></a></div>Dancing in the sunshine, Los Porcos mixes up everything that’s good about its members’ musical make up. Despite Soundcloud declaring they come from “<i>New Pork City</i>” the line-up is actually made of seven London and Manchester natives and members of <i>Profundo</i> and <i>FAMY </i>as well as the now defunct Wu Lyf, each bringing their own sound to the fore. Los Porcos’ seamlessly combines the cloudy dream popped melodies of FAMY with the weighty psych-rock riffs of Wu Lyf but with a completely fresh nu-disco funk twist. A band to watch: rely on these guys to keep your Summer going smooth, well into the autumn.<br/><br/>The tracks will be released via Limited Edition 12" and digitally on 15th September through <a href="http://www.caledoniarecords.bigcartel.com/" target="_blank"><b>Caledonia Records</b></a> / <a href="http://losporcos.com/" target="_blank"><b>Los Porcos</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div>||
ALBUM: MAYORS OF MIYAZAKI - HOLY COP|<div style="text-align: justify;">Brat punk. The exuberance of youth pouring out of every jutting note and shouty verse. Adolescence is both a celebrated freedom and an angst-ridden cross to bear for those in this genre. They’re young, they’re twee, they’re happy. They’re sad, they’re hurt, they’re self-harmy. Such personal turmoil is expressed in an oddly uniform way across the genre considering it comprises of people seemingly angry about conformity and the need for self expression. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Mostly, it’s dual vocals that yap and protest whilst angular guitars jab out math riffs that burst into poppy digressions now and again. Here’s a twisted guitar riff that <i>Battles</i> would be proud of. Here’s a sing along chorus that <i>Johnny Foreigner</i> would love. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Here’s an album by <b>Mayors of Miyazaki</b> called <b>Holy Cop</b>. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">You can’t help but feel this brat punk, angular, indie rock genre has sailed, disappeared over the horizon, hit an iceberg and is coming back to us in dribs and drabs as flotsam and jetsam. Yet it’s not Mayors of Miyazaki’s fault they’re struggling to stay afloat on an ex-boat. Or genre. Or something. “<i>I didn’t ask to be born!</i>” they might exclaim, before eating their dinner in their bedroom, rather than at the dining table with the rest of the family. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">You see, this music has been done and then done some more. The yearning, burning, churning of urgent, angular notes and jerky vocals, the endless switching between the purposely obtuse and the accessibly pop. The duel vocal shrill, the 7/8 time signature, <i>The Automatic</i>, <i>Dananananaykroyd</i>; whatever. Dynastically, this record is a carbon copy of the genre’s forefathers. A predictable romp at best. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Holy Cop</b> conjures up the summer nights of youth, the burn of teenage love and the unrepentant loyalty of your equally youthful friends. It’s all painted here in broad strokes. Broad indeed, as chopping up this album into individual tracks is a baffling challenge. It’s a giant, continuous smear of meandering notes, staccato rhythms and shouty choruses.Saying that, the celebratory jangle of ‘<b>Tongues</b>’ is more poppy and enjoyable than most, whilst the <i>Sleigh Bells</i> style ‘<b>Human Resources</b>’ is a mouth-wateringly jagged and turbulent ride. The wonderful head nodding and groovy riff on ‘<b>Parts per Million</b>’ is stand out, whilst ‘<b>Dry Palm</b>’ has reverberations of 80s post punk pop and the monstrous ‘<b>Muy Sexo</b>’ is a stomping, awesomely swollen riff that could be in any number of gangster movies. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">This album seems, at first glance, uninspiring if only for its formulaic predictability. It appears dated and oddly naive. There are moments that, probably in their bid to be different, sound like everything from the last decade. The closing track is guilty as charged, for example. But in this haystack of fiddly guitarisms and half riffs, of barking, spluttered vocal lines and a million drum fills, is a charm, an identity, a odd idiosyncratic quirk that draws you in. The naivety becomes welcoming, a permission to let go of pretension, an instruction to just fucking enjoy yourself. Ok, so Holy Cop isn’t all good but it isn’t all bad either. Its weaknesses are perversely its strengths. It’s hedonistic goofiness turned up to 11. And that alone, is worth checking out. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/><b><a href="http://mayorsofmiyazaki.bandcamp.com/album/holy-cop" target="_blank">Holy Cop</a></b> is out now. // <b><a href="http://www.mayorsofmiyazaki.blogspot.co.uk/" target="_blank">Mayors Of Miyazaki</a></b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"></div>||
EP: SOPHIE JAMIESON - WHERE|<div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-FsTap9gfdDo/UgFmfzkpb5I/AAAAAAAAEy8/TnGng0KLsTs/s1600/971782_536302166410990_778626003_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="258" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-FsTap9gfdDo/UgFmfzkpb5I/AAAAAAAAEy8/TnGng0KLsTs/s320/971782_536302166410990_778626003_n.jpg" width="320"/></a>'<b>Where</b>' is the softly spoken debut EP from <b>Sophie Jamieson</b> which was released through <b>Folkroom Records </b>at the end of June.<br/><br/>Having recently played a series of live shows including the <i>To Kill a King</i> stage at London's quickest growing, not for profit event <i>Leefest</i>, this Cambridge educated folk musician has gained nods of approval from across blogging networks and the online music scene, as well as featuring on radio stations across London, including independent music lovers <i>BBC 6 Music</i>.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Along with <i>Ben Walker</i> (electric guitar, bass, programming), <i>Derek Yau </i>(cello) and <i>Liam Hoflay</i> (electric guitar) Jamieson's music fills shady silences with pensive waves of stillness. She makes gently breathing melodies with soft instrumentation, lifted with cello and electronic nuances, while her vocals lift and fall from heady breaths to strong expressive, full bodied notes. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ZOVns5yNFJo/UgFTD1S8a_I/AAAAAAAAEys/GC-UrwN3F1E/s1600/a1647355723_2.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-ZOVns5yNFJo/UgFTD1S8a_I/AAAAAAAAEys/GC-UrwN3F1E/s320/a1647355723_2.jpg" width="320"/></a>Opening and stand-out track '<b>Waterloo</b>' sends silent shocks of melody through the '<i>crowds of waterloo</i>' repeating the refrain and EP title questioning '<i>where are we going to</i>?' Finger style guitar and sustained cello with subtle electronic instrumentation add body to this pensive sound. In '<b>Dinah</b>' Jamieson's acoustic guitar riffs stand out on this soulfully soft and introspective folksy tune  with delicate melodies harmonising with classical touches in the instrumentation. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>I Don't</b>' has the added drama of deep resonating drum beats and fervid cello vibrato that add to the melodic shifts and lulls. '<b>Ode to the East</b>' is hymn-like in contrast and reminiscent of the quieter moments of <i>The Cranberries</i>. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Folk is always in danger of falling through the cracks of dull repetitiveness, but there is just enough emotional and instrumental tension within this EP to keep a dreaming listener entranced. This is music like flickering candlelight, to lie still, to think and to feel to.<br/><br/><a href="https://www.facebook.com/sophiejamiesonmusic" target="_blank"><b>Sophie Jamieson</b></a> // <a href="http://www.folkroomrecords.bandcamp.com/album/where-ep" target="_blank"><b>'Where' EP</b></a> // <a href="http://www.folkroomrecords.bandcamp.com/" target="_blank"><b>Folkroom Records</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="https://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F96389359" width="100%"></iframe></div>||
SINGLE: GINA CIMMELLI - CLEMENTINE|<div style="text-align: justify;">Every so often I become fairly disillusioned with the acoustic singer songwriter genre. Personally I like my acoustic music to be just that, acoustic. Stripped back, mainly letting the guitar, vocals, and lyrics do their thing. Unfortunately there seems to be an increasingly common approach for acoustic artists to quickly shun their rawer roots in favour of a bigger, more in your face production that leans more to pop music than it does acoustic. (<i>Gabrielle Aplin</i> is an example - for me her early work far outshines the debut record which the masses have so far gobbled up this year but left me fairly disappointed).</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Which today leads us to <b>Gina Cimmelli</b>, a Brookyln based singer songwriter who oozes talent, confindence, and a clear appreication of how powerful her gentle, yet alluring music can be. '<b>Clementine</b>' is the first of three tracks which will make up her latest EP which is due to be released this Summer.<br/><br/>The track has a beautiful arrangement throughout, with Cimmelli's vocals a clear standout - her voice is tantalizingly fragile yet assured, and overall the track has lovely warm feeling. Imagine a slowed down Best Coast crossed with First Aid it and The Staves and you're getting somewhere close. Keep your ears out for the next single 'Like I Did', which we can tell you is equally fantastic!</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://ginaspictureshow.com/" target="_blank"><b>GINA CIMMELLI</b></a></div>||
