SINGLE: DANIEL JAMES - THE STONE AND THE HOLLOW|<div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>The Stone and The Hollow</b>' is the new track from London based singer songwriter <b>Daniel James</b>. It follows the release of his debut track '<b>Jackdraw</b>' earlier in the year. Daniel, who is from Northern Ireland, said about the track that "<i>it was inspired by memories of  walks around Belfast Lough and how that felt different to the new London landscape I found myself in. Time to think and ponder on new and old relationships alike, all compounded by the differing sense of space I felt.</i>"</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The track is sparse, with James singing around a simple beat, piano loop, and acoustic guitar, but this only helps to shine the focus upon his vocals and lyrics which are the clear stand out. His voice is definitive and carries a poignancy that enforces the themes behind his words. Think a more sprightly<i> James Blake</i> cross between a slightly more downbeat <i>Benjamin Francis Leftwich</i>, cut across <i>Alt-J</i> beats. One to certainly look out for this year.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://thisisdanieljames.tumblr.com/" target="_blank"><b>Daniel James</b></a> // <a href="http://www.facebook.com/ThisisdanielJames" target="_blank"><b>Facebook</b></a> // <a href="https://twitter.com/iamdanieljames" target="_blank"><b>Twitter</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b> </b><span class="ecxApple-style-span" style="font-family: Arial; font-size: 13px;"><br/></span></div>||
ALBUM: LORE CITY - ABSENCE & TIME|<div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Lore City</b> are not the kind of band to take things lightly. Their dark and emotive music absorbs and revels in all that is melancholic and tumultuous in life. Their music is a giant lament to the bittersweet nature of existence. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Their debut album ‘<b>Absence and Time</b>’ isn't the kind of catchy record to sling on the stereo whilst cooking dinner, it’s a painful work of love and demands attention. It’s not a dip in and dip out record, it’s an all or nothing affair and somehow, Lore City convey all this with half an opening track. ‘<b>Keep</b>’ is the kind of epic sorrow that commands respect; like the <i>Smiths ‘How Soon Is Now’</i> or any other great, atmospheric song about how it hurts to live. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Yet, this is no emo album. This isn't about high school popularity, body confidence or haircuts. <b>Laura Mariposaʼs</b> vocal acrobatics puts paid to that idea. At times she is soft and nurturing, at others slurry and drunk with woe, like a well meaning but ultimately unfit mother. Sometimes, like  on the psychedelic tipped ‘<b>Whole Lot</b>’, she is positively psychotic, a screaming banshee, yelling along to a singular reverb soaked guitar. Like <i>Zola Jesus</i> or a latter day <i>Grace Slick</i>, she is profound in her declaration to the world. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-e-vJTtTvMOI/UW8HVkspEsI/AAAAAAAAEtk/rzhVCmw962o/s1600/658008886-1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="212" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-e-vJTtTvMOI/UW8HVkspEsI/AAAAAAAAEtk/rzhVCmw962o/s320/658008886-1.jpg" width="320"/></a>Of course, musician and artistic partner in the band <b>Eric Bessel</b> must also take equal credit and blame for this heady creation. Looking a bit like a bespectacled lawyer or promising, number crunching prodigy in an accountancy firm, he confounds expectations by skilfully creating ominous soundscapes for Mariposa to play with and manipulate. Moaning guitars, elongated, rumbling bass lines and warm, atmospheric hums all wallpaper a backdrop of night time deserts, outstretched roads and the kind of creeping skin touch of reality that only comes in the depths of the night. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">All this might sound ludicrously pretentious, but Lore City aren’t here to entertain, they’re here for your soul. Simplicity is their forte. With droll, plodding drum lines <i>Meg White</i> would scoff at, the shimmering loop of a single guitar strum, the wail of a lonely, anguished vocal and the empty chasms of time between beats all strike their own, resonating chord. Closing track ‘<b>Fortuneless Fortune</b>’ displays all these traits with the kind of idiosyncratic flare that it’s only taken a mere eight tracks to fall in love with. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">This album is an esoteric, existential and enlightened work of art that operates on a different plain to its contemporaries - if it has any. Truly great from opening bass drum kick to closing guitar strum. Hold on in there, it’s going to get bumpy. // <b><a href="http://www.lorecitymusic.com/" target="_blank">Lore City</a></b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div>||
EP: LONDON GRAMMAR - METAL & DUST|<div style="text-align: justify;">So far not much is known about <b>London Grammar</b>, apart from them being a 3-piece (<i>Hannah</i>, <i>Daniel</i>, and <i>Dot</i>), and that their debut release, a 4 track EP titled '<b>Metal &amp; Dust</b>' is out right now digitally and on 7".</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Our attention was first drawn to the track '<b>Hey Now</b>', a quiet, dark song that gently simmers along almost unnoticed but easily catches you off guard during its relatively short length of 3.27. The vocals are clearly the first point of notice, with Hannah's depth and range standing out, but the electronic based music behind is also interesting, with the use of space, tempo, ambiance, and repetition quite alluring. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Title track '<b>Metal &amp; Dust</b>' is more up tempo, with the beats turned up front and centre, whilst '<b>Darling Are You Gonna Leave Me</b>' has a gentle, party feel to it, with certain parts a bit reminiscent of <i>Ellie Goulding</i> from her debut record. The EP ends with a <i>Dot Major</i> remix of 'Hey Now' which only goes to further strengthen the effectiveness of the track and EP as a whole.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">There's plenty of reference points on this EP, with the likes of <i>The XX</i>, <i>James Blake</i>, <i>Egyptian Hip-Hop</i>, <i>Alt-J</i>, <i>Mt Wolf</i> and other ethereal electronic pop artists that seem to surround the airwaves at the minute all being picked up on, but there's also enough ideas and invention to suggest London Grammar have a clear voice of their own. We hear a debut album is in the pipeline and by accounts could be something rather special if this EP is anything to go.<br/><br/>Buy the Metal &amp; Dust' EP from <a href="http://smarturl.it/metalanddust" target="_blank"><b>iTunes</b></a> or the <a href="http://www.normanrecords.com/records/138902-london-grammar--metal-" target="_blank"><b>7"</b></a> now. // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/londongrammar" target="_blank"><b>London Grammar</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div>||
EP REVIEW: ANNIE DRESSNER - EAST TWENTIES|<div style="text-align: justify;">Whilst the slew of twee female singer-songwriters continues to be ever present in our mailbag, it does mean that finding those needles in the hack-stack has become quite a joy. The latest sharp point to stand out is American <b>Annie Dressner</b>.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">She's from New York City but moved to the UK last year, which was presumably not for our weather. In 2011 she released her debut album '<i>Strangers Who Knew Each Other's Names</i>', and has played numerous live venues both in New York, and across the UK since her move here. April 8th sees the release of her latest body of work, an EP titled '<b>East Twenties</b>', which is co produced with <i>Paul Goodwin</i>.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The EP begins with '<b>Heartbreaker</b>', a song which lyrically deals with that well trodden sad subject, yet musically things are joyously upbeat, with warm sounding guitars and percussion, quite a lovely juxtaposition. Her vocal delivery throughout the record is almost conversational, allowing you to feel a sense of easy understanding and knowing of her songs. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>I Can't Forget</b>' is a touching song that delicately deals with the feeling of loss, with the sincerity of Dressner's vocals shining as well as a beautiful cello emanating throughout. '<b>Flame</b>' is the shortest track on the record at just over two and a half minutes, yet is feels the most full bodied of the songs put forward. '<b>Lost In A Car</b>' closes things out in poignant fashion, dealing with more of life's troublesome issues, with Dressner's soft voice and delicate guitar proving hard to not get swept up by.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>East Twenties</b>' is a record which makes you consider those events which have gone before you, taking you on a somewhat nostalgic journey through feelings which are most probably negative and upsetting. Yet the way in which <b>Annie Dressner </b>presents these four songs is refreshing, with her approachable style and musically upbeat nature leaves you with a positive feeling in the end.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">You can pre-order 'East Twenties through Annie's <a href="http://www.pledgemusic.com/projects/anniedressner" target="_blank"><b>Pledge Music</b></a> page and catch her at the EP launch on the 9th April at <a href="http://www.wegottickets.com/pulluptheroots/event/200739" target="_blank"><b>Slaughtered Lamb</b></a> in London. // <a href="http://www.anniedressner.com/" target="_blank"><b>Annie Dressner</b></a></div>||
EP REVIEW: MT. WOLF - HYPOLIGHT|<div style="text-align: justify;">London four-piece <b>Mt Wolf </b>will be no stranger to those who frequent the music blogging world on a consistent basis, with their EP from last year '<b>Life Size Ghosts</b>' featuring favourably on many sites across the board. Our friends over at <b><a href="http://www.fadedglamour.co.uk/" target="_blank"><i>Faded Glamour</i></a></b> said that "<span class="text_exposed_show"><i>the band have recently been compared to the now Mercury Music Prize winning Alt-J - (and) it's perfectly conceivable that Mt. Wolf will reach such equally great heights.</i>" </span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span class="text_exposed_show">High praise and expectation then for a band who only came together at the start of 2012, which is only heightened when names such as <i>James Blake</i>, <i>Sigur Ros</i>, and <i>The XX</i> are thrown in by others as similar acts. But upon listening to their new EP '<b>Hypolight</b>' it's actually quite easy to see where all the hype and fuss is justifiably from. Describing themselves as '<i>dream folk</i>' on their <a href="https://www.facebook.com/MtWolfOfficial" target="_blank"><b>facebook</b></a>, it's instantly clear that the rather ambiguous new fangled genre is probably about right for them. Beginning with the title track '<b>Hypolight</b>' we have the floaty acoustic guitars intertwined with electronic synths, before the star of the show/ep/album/record steps up the mic in the form of vocalist <b>Kate Sproule</b>. With a voice that seemingly has a multitude of ranges, she controls everything almost effortlessly, which seemingly does put you in a dream like state, so its '<i>dream folk</i>' then, obviously. </span><br/><br/><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-HvEIAUtbCNs/UVDOGo4Dj-I/AAAAAAAAEsk/B8jJPSE_cME/s1600/ImageProxy.mvc.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="240" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-HvEIAUtbCNs/UVDOGo4Dj-I/AAAAAAAAEsk/B8jJPSE_cME/s320/ImageProxy.mvc.jpg" width="320"/></a></div><span class="text_exposed_show">'<b>Veins</b>' carries on in a similar style, the music sounding like it's being stretched like a time lapse video, with Sproule again leading things with her powerful vocals. This time around the music has bit more leadtime, with the <i>Alt-J</i> references becoming more apparent as the guitar/electronic combination is played out well, with that feeling of genres clashing against and then with each other hard to ignore. </span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span class="text_exposed_show">Lead single '<b>Shapeshift</b>' is perhaps the most complete song on the record, featuring a glorious throbbing beat throughout over which Sproule again impresses with her great depth, with the delicate yet commanding vocals leaving a lasting impression. The accompanying <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eIkWI3PsESI&amp;feature=player_embedded" target="_blank"><b>video</b></a> is also worth a look with the simple black and white shots and slow motion effects working to great effect. The EP closes with a cover of <i>Usher's</i> '<b>Climax</b>', which is a more stripped backed approach, which only goes to further enhance the vocal delights of that lady again (<b>Kate Sproule</b> if you didn't know), who has such temperament with her voice it's quite astonishing. She can effect a range of feelings with only the slightest of changes, which you can hardly pick up on during the songs its all done so naturally and seamlessly. </span><br/><br/><span class="text_exposed_show"><b>Hypolight</b> is a strong, dominant record that suggests greater things are indeed ahead for this young four-piece from London. We will certainly watch and listen to their development with keen interest over the time to come.</span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span class="text_exposed_show"><b>Hypolight</b> is available through <a href="http://twosistersrecords.co.uk/" target="_blank"><b>Two Sisters Records</b></a> on April 8th. <a href="http://www.mtwolf.co.uk/" target="_blank"><b>Mt. Wolf</b></a> // <a href="https://itunes.apple.com/gb/album/hypolight-ep/id615366262" target="_blank"><b>Pre-Order 'Hypolight' on iTunes</b></a></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"></div>||
NEW MUSIC: BLOODY MAMMALS - MADAM|<div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Bloody Mammals</b> are a post hardcore 4 piece from London, who in May will release their debut mini-album '<b>Eventually Your House Will Burn Down</b>' through <b>49s Vs Dolphins</b> and <b>Flatpack Recordings</b>. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Taken from said album is '<b>Madam</b>', a frenetic two and a half minutes of controlled mayhem - you could think <i>Comeback Kid</i>, <i>La Dispute</i> and <i>Touche Amore</i>, but with a quintessentially British vibe emanating throughout. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">It's refreshing to hear such aptitude for their craft from a band this side of the pond - it's fair to say we are expecting big things from the mini record when that drops later this year! </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Pre-order '<b>Eventually Your Horse Will Burn</b>' through <a href="http://bloodymammals.bandcamp.com/album/eventually-your-house-will-burn-down" target="_blank"><b>Bandcamp</b></a> // <a href="http://bloodymammals.com/" target="_blank"><b>Bloody Mammals</b></a></div>||
INTERVIEW: SUNSHINE|<div style="text-align: justify;">We recently reviewed the debut self titled album from our favourite Canadian band of 2013 - <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/2013/02/album-sunshine-sunshine.html" target="_blank"><b>Sunshine</b></a>. We thought it would be a great idea to catch up with the guys to discuss them, their album, and whatever else comes to mind.<br/><br/>Many thanks to <i>Gillian Damborg</i>, <i>Trevor Risk</i>, <i>Tyler Quarles</i>, <i>Ian Urbansk</i>i,  and <i>Sean Tyson</i> aka the <i>Yamaha RX5</i> (just watch the video to understand that one), for giving us their time, thoughts, and a large sprinkling of laughs.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">It is also a <b>Music Liberation</b> first, as we bring you their answers in the form of images and sound combined, a video interview no less! (It's only taken us the 6 years to get there...)</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Questions: <b>Sarah Rayner</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Editor: <b>Jon Sidwell</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Filmed: March 2013 by <b>Owen Ellis</b> and <b>Sunshine</b><br/><br/></div>||
ALBUM: FIDLAR - FIDLAR|<div style="text-align: justify;">Let’s get this out of the way first: <b>Fidlar's</b> name is an acronym for '<i>Fuck It Dog, Life's a Risk</i>’. Make of that what you will, but it’s certainly a good indicator of the band’s eccentric fratboy approach to their craft. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Chaotic self-titled debut '<b>FIDLAR</b>' is one long ode to partying and over consumption. This unique brand of scrappy surf-punk noise makes them sound like the raucous younger siblings of <i>The Vaccines</i> or a very drunk <i>Japandroids</i>; but these guys aren’t nostalgic about the times they've had, they’re living them, right here, right now and you’re going to hear about it whether you want to or not.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">“<i>I DRINK CHEAP BEER SO WHAT FUCK YOU</i>” bellows the chorus of opening track and lead single ‘<b>Cheap Beer</b>’. ‘<i>There’s nothing wrong living like this, all my friends are pieces of shit</i>’ they declare on ‘<b>Stoked and Broke</b>’. Only two songs in and the band have already firmly nailed their colours to the mast of over indulgence and self destruction.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Whilst FIDLAR pull no punches in who they are and what they do, they’re representing a lifestyle that is nothing new. In fact the <i>live fast die young</i> attitude is a monstrous cliche that most discerning new bands try to avoid. Yet there is a certain gleeful stupidity to this LA foursome’s reckless abandon. They fly in the face of the bookish introspection of today’s indie rock. Each song is an unpretentious slice of shouty power punk that exists for the sake of existing. There’s no deeper meaning other than a hat-tip to the joys of excess.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>FIDLAR’s</b> debut is a simple and surprisingly catchy record that becomes more than the sum of its individual songs by unwittingly representing a sense of fun that has been all but weeded out of new guitar music today. And for that alone, this record is well worth a listen. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">It is out now through <a href="http://www.momandpoprecords.com/" target="_blank"><b>Mom and Pop Records</b></a> // <b><a href="http://www.fidlarmusic.com/" target="_blank">Fidlar</a></b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div>||
INTERVIEW: VOICES|<div style="text-align: justify;">Another of the acts we recently nominated for the <b>Glastonbury Emerging Talent</b> stage (alongside <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/2013/02/interview-esper-scout.html" target="_blank"><i><b>Esper Scout</b></i></a> and <b>Moats</b>) were <b>Voices</b>. The melodic post-hardcore band from Hertfordshire were kind enough to answer some of our probing, and some of our not so probing, interview questions.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">To view the full long-list of 120 acts that made it through to the next stage of the competition, as well as all the blogs that took part in the voting process, head over <a href="http://www.glastonburyfestivals.co.uk/news/2013-emerging-talent-competition-longlist-announced" target="_blank"><b>here</b></a>. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Q1. Congratulations on getting through to the next stage of the Glastonbury Emerging Talent stage! What made you apply for this competition? How do you feel about making it through? </b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Even though we're not necessarily suited to the normal Glastonbury scene of bands we will hopefully be trying to bring something new and different to the table, it'll be interesting to find out the response to our tracks and therefore we're incredibly happy that we managed to get through to the long-list, its a great opportunity and a brilliant competition." </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Q2. Where are you guys from? How did you meet? </b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"We are from St. Albans, Hertfordshire, homes of bands such as<i> Enter Shikari</i>, <i>Your Demise</i> and <i>Friendly Fires</i>. We met through secondary school and decided to make a band, and from then on we passed through phases of death metal in which we wrote about the devil and the ascension of a demon from hell, to writing post-hardcore style music, which allowed us to wrote more heartfelt music. We have been together for five years now and despite changes in our line up we have carried on strong." </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Q3. Describe your music in three words? </b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Dissonant, melodic, meaningful." </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Q4. Who are your musical and non-musical influences? </b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Between us we're pretty heavily influenced by <i>Every Time I Die</i>, <i>Bring Me The Horizon</i>, <i>Letlive</i>, and <i>La Dispute</i>. There are also lots of electronica/atmospheric elements too! Non-musical influences are pretty broad; we like to think we have something to say in our music so in that sense we're interested in exploring certain elements of the world we live in...or think we live in. *init*" </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-igZQT2NDvjo/UTUKmtGnf2I/AAAAAAAAEq0/4MrEmE1UEnk/s1600/479696_527427720624459_523843705_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="319" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-igZQT2NDvjo/UTUKmtGnf2I/AAAAAAAAEq0/4MrEmE1UEnk/s320/479696_527427720624459_523843705_n.jpg" width="320"/></a><b>Q5. What's on your agenda for 2013? </b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"We've got a load of stuff on the horizon which we're very very excited about. We've got our second self-recorded album (<b><i>Sleepers and Dreamers</i></b>) on its way in Summer and with it a video! Plus we're currently sorting out merchandise orders... all pretty stressful, but well worth it! (All details on the facebook!)" </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Q6. Any new bands/artists you recommend us checking out? </b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Really liking a band called <i>Shields</i> at the moment, you can find them on <a href="http://www.facebook.com/Shieldsuk" target="_blank">facebook</a>, and <i><a href="http://www.facebook.com/ChangeOfPlan" target="_blank">Change Of Plan</a></i> are our boys from back home. Also, if you haven't heard of them already I'd recommend checking out both <i>CityLightThief</i> and <i>La Dispute</i>. Neither are 'new' but neither are hugely well known." </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Q7. If you could tour with any two artists, past or present, who would they be and why?</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"<i>At The Drive In</i> and <i>The Cat Empire</i>! At The Drive In for the destructive action, and The Cat Empire for the trumpets! Although, to be fair, I doubt the latter would have us!" </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-qdW-F1IPP38/UTUJN2pV1BI/AAAAAAAAEqs/55ZBGeGl_fo/s1600/263933_474044509296114_127953859_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="212" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-qdW-F1IPP38/UTUJN2pV1BI/AAAAAAAAEqs/55ZBGeGl_fo/s320/263933_474044509296114_127953859_n.jpg" width="320"/></a><b>Q8. What 3 things would you have on your perfect tour rider? </b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">1. <i>Kale</i> - A Superfood that Max and Osh are heavily addicted to </div><div style="text-align: justify;">2. <i>Blender</i> - To blend the Kale to a pulp </div><div style="text-align: justify;">3. <i>Ginger &amp; Fruits</i> - To put in the Kale shake </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Q9. Aside from the world of music, what do you get up to?</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Well some of us are at university so that's obviously time consuming! We come from a background of skateboarding and gig-going so lots of that still happens. Osh and Rob are in a little acoustic outfit known as <i>Sparrow Prince</i>, and Laurie produces electronic music under the alias <i>Clamblem</i>. Max is also a professional hand model. Matty isn't." </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Q10. How can we find out more about you? </b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">We're all over the regular social media sites - <a href="http://twitter.com/VoicesTweet" target="_blank">twitter</a>, <a href="http://www.facebook.com/voicesbanduk" target="_blank">facebook</a>, <a href="http://www.soundcloud.com/voicesuk" target="_blank">soundcloud</a>, or you could come to a show, all of our dates can be found on our Facebook page! Or just shoot us an email: <a href="mailto:voicesuk@live.com">voicesuk@live.com</a><a href="mailto:voicesuk@live.com" target="_blank">voicesuk@live.com</a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><i><b>Many thanks to the guys in Voices for answering our questions! Best of luck to them in the next stage of the competition!</b></i></div><div style="text-align: justify;">  </div>||
INTERVIEW: ESPER SCOUT|<div style="text-align: justify;">We recently put forward <b>Esper Scout</b> for the <b>Emerging Talent Stage</b> at this year's <b>Glastonbury Festival</b>, along with <b>Moats</b>, and <b>Voices</b>. We thought it would be a great idea to find out a little more about them, so we spoke with Sarah, Kirsty, Rebecca, and Lou from the band. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">To view the full long-list of 120 acts that made it through to the next stage of the competition, as well as all the blogs that took part in the voting process, head over <a href="http://www.glastonburyfestivals.co.uk/news/2013-emerging-talent-competition-longlist-announced" target="_blank"><b>here</b></a>.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b><span lang="EN-GB">Q1. Congratulations on getting throughto the next stage of the GlastonburyEmerging Talent stage! What made you apply for this competition? How do youfeel about making it through?</span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><b>Sarah(guitar, vocals)</b>: "I was spurred on through separate recommendations from twoof our friends who are both passionate about the band and love <i>Glastonbury</i>. Ididn’t tell the rest of <b>Esper Scout</b> and so finding out that we’d been selected forthe long-list was an extra surprise for them!"</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><b>Kirsty(guitar)</b>: "Obvious to say we’re flattered! It feels like we’ve been working hardrecently and it seems to be paying off. This is a really great opportunity,even if it just means that one or two extra people hear about us."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b><span lang="EN-GB">Q2. Where are you guys from? How did youmeet?</span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-BYJkGmsVw9A/US9hRB9AcbI/AAAAAAAAEmk/KVi4sg1Q56Q/s1600/esperScoutMain.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="176" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-BYJkGmsVw9A/US9hRB9AcbI/AAAAAAAAEmk/KVi4sg1Q56Q/s320/esperScoutMain.jpg" width="320"/></a></div><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Arial;"><b>Sarah:</b>"We’re based in Leeds but Kirsty, Rebecca and I were born, raised and met inManchester, actually our town is appropriately called Bury. Me and Kirsty endedup sat next to each other on a school coach trip to Germany and shared mixtapes. I’ve never realised before how poetic that could sound and I guess itis! When we got home I decided to pursue drums and she picked up the bass andguitar." (<i>ED: aww that's awesome!</i>)</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Arial;"><b>Kirsty:</b>"Yeah, at first it was just so you’d have someone to play with. Turned outalright."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Arial;"><b>Sarah:</b> "Thanksfor doing that! How I ended up singing and playing guitar in a band I’m notquite sure. After some ‘can I/can’t I?’ deliberation in the beginning I feelthat something’s definitely started clicking between the four of us over thepast year and writing and self-demoing for our mini-album which we’re recordingin Spring has given us an injection of confidence."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Arial;"><b>Rebecca(bass):</b> "Yeah definitely. The three of us moved up to Leeds in 2008 without muchof a plan and met Lou through the city’s network of musicians. We’ve been writingand playing together since then but Esper Scout only came in to being a coupleof years ago through changes in line-up and finding a collective and betterfocused mind-set."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b><span lang="EN-GB">Q3. Describe your music in three words?</span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><b>Lou(drums)</b>: "‘Loud/Quiet/Rock’ says everything about us and nothing at the sametime."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b><span lang="EN-GB">Q4. Who are your musical and non-musicalinfluences?</span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB"><b>Sarah:</b> "I thinkyou can hear reflections of dynamic, melodic guitar and drum driven bands likeThrice, Silversun Pickups and Alexisonfire in our songs. My most prizedpossession is a ‘Rap Band’ beatbox machine which plays half a dozen electronicdrum patterns depending on what buttons you press. An Uncle bought it me forChristmas when I was six and apparently I sat there for days pressing differentcombinations of three buttons which, as much as they say they were happy forme, must have driven my family and their friends a bit bonkers."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB"><b>Lou: </b>"I neverlooked up to anyone in particular when I started playing as much as I think Ijust felt a natural draw to drumming; a compulsion to build and elaborate onbeats. I found out that my Granddad used to play and he was a well-respectedman which inspired me to keep on at it through admiration for him."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB"><b>Rebecca:</b> "What weseem to have in common is that we all found an interest in sound before weidentified specific music or artists we liked. Non-musically, seeing injusticeand imbalance when it comes to female rights first motivated me to pick up thebass. From a young age I felt strongly about women becoming as empowered as menand it made me realise how important it is to have your voice heard which inturn has influenced me artistically and expressively."</span><br/><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-RN_i_udVxYc/US9hhH1RWXI/AAAAAAAAEms/E9W18VStNOE/s1600/562856_388611534516708_325670059_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="267" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-RN_i_udVxYc/US9hhH1RWXI/AAAAAAAAEms/E9W18VStNOE/s640/562856_388611534516708_325670059_n.jpg" width="640"/></a></div><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b><span lang="EN-GB">Q5. What's onyour agenda for 2013?</span></b><span lang="EN-GB"> </span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB"><b>Kirsty:</b> "We’vebeen asked to play Not Woodstock festival in Northumberland which is takingplace at Featherstone castle 3 miles south of Hadrian’s Wall. Me, Rebecca andSarah are visiting the USA’s West Coast in May and we’re hoping to play a bitwhilst we’re out there. Open mics, guitar shops, wherever will have us!"</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB"><b>Lou: </b>"We’ve justfinished demo-ing our mini-album so after recording the six songs properly inthe studio we’ll be busy with mixing and all the other things associated with arelease such as videos, singles etc. Most importantly we’ll be playing somegigs in support of them, including a week down south which we’re excited about."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b><span lang="EN-GB">Q6. Any new bands/artists you recommendus checking out?</span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-tKNhn7x_nMg/US9iwIv4sZI/AAAAAAAAEm0/Sk7ZUadlC9M/s1600/601078_517912894919904_116177793_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-tKNhn7x_nMg/US9iwIv4sZI/AAAAAAAAEm0/Sk7ZUadlC9M/s320/601078_517912894919904_116177793_n.jpg" width="212"/></a></div><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><b>Sarah:</b> "Withus being based in Leeds you don’t have to look far to find great bands.Festivals like<i> British Wildlife</i>, which takes place at the Brudenell Social Club,and Live at Leeds, show just how high the quality of music is in the city is,both in terms of ideas and passion. <i>Bearfoot Beware</i>, <i>ENVOYS</i>, <i>British RacingGreen</i> and <i>Insatellites</i>, for example, who are all currently working on excitingthings. We’re really lucky to be able to be part such a well-connected andencouraging community of musicians, videographers, writers, graphic artists andillustrators etc., the coming together of which is aided by the newly openedLeeds Music Hub which is quickly becoming an invaluable resource."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><b>Rebecca:</b>"There are always at least three or four decent gigs a week across a wide scopeof genres. Venues like <i>Wharf Chambers</i> and the <i>Brudenell</i> are really passionateabout the bands they put on and how they treat audiences."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><b>Lou:</b> "Werecently invited our friends<i> Kassassin Street</i> from Portsmouth to play with usand they are one of the best live bands I’ve ever seen. We wouldn’t besurprised if they did well for themselves this year." </span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b><span lang="EN-GB">Q7. If youcould tour with any two artists, past or present, who would they be and why?</span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><b>Kirsty:</b> "It’s been a dream of mine for ages totour with the <i>Bloodhound Gang</i> around Europe on their party bus. We’d need tobring some ear defenders and eye mask for Lou. The girl’s gotta sleep."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><b>Lou:</b> And a cycle helmet so nobody shaves myhair off. Nobody wants a Lou with a head-chill!</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b><span lang="EN-GB">Q8. What 3things would you have on your perfect tour rider?</span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"></div><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><b>Sarah:</b> "I think I can speak for myself and Rebwhen I say porridge oats and marrowfat peas. Those actually might be a pain toprepare without a hob, so that’d be my third request. Am I asking too much?I’ll probably bring my own camping stove then, and a pan."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB"><b>Rebecca:</b> "Addbananas to the porridge and you’ve got yourself a treat for any time of day."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB"><b>Lou: </b>"Cleansocks, a book of arrow-words and Diet Coke."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB"><b>Kirsty: </b>"Beer andtwiglets. We chose more than three but on average less than three each if thatcounts."</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b><span lang="EN-GB">Q9. Asidefrom the world of music, what do you get up to?</span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><b>Rebecca:</b> "Some of us get out cycling andrunning along Leeds-Liverpool canal and the forest near our base in Leeds. Abit of travelling too, when time and funds allow!"</span></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><b><span lang="EN-GB">Q10. How canwe find out more about you?</span></b></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><b>Sarah: </b>"Our main site is <a href="http://www.esperscout.com/">www.esperscout.com</a> for news and music,with all external links accessible through icons at the top of the page."</span><br/><br/><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"><u>Interviewer: <b>Jon Sidwell </b></u></span><br/><br/><i><span lang="EN-GB" style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Many thanks to Sarah, Kirsty, Rebacca, and Lou for taking time out to talk us here at <b>Music Liberation</b>. We wish them luck in the next stage of the competition!</span></i><br/><br/></div>||
ALBUM: TORRES - TORRES|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-9Gc0iWKRyNc/USKkpCp16jI/AAAAAAAAEas/8pcdSf3CQD4/s1600/155928_136452936506762_2042860661_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-9Gc0iWKRyNc/USKkpCp16jI/AAAAAAAAEas/8pcdSf3CQD4/s320/155928_136452936506762_2042860661_n.jpg" width="320"/></a></div><i>Mackenzie Scott</i> is <b>Torres</b>, a young 22 year lady from Nashville, Tennessee, who earlier last month released her debut self titled album. Like most solo singer songwriters she has a story, however hers is somewhat more believable and that only adds an extra dimension to what is a deftly strong opening body of work.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">We are told that is was during the Christmas of 2011 that Scott was given her first electric guitar - a <i>Gibson 335</i> for you guitar heads out there, which was a present from her family. With it she discovered that her previously acoustic based songs could take on a whole new form, growing into the ten songs which form her debut LP.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Opener '<b>Mother Earth, Father Good</b>' starts with some sombre strings, before a distorted guitar is added alongside Scott's solemn vocals. This rather melancholy beginning might instantly make you feel like there's going to be great depth to this album; well you wouldn't be wrong. As soon as '<b>Honey</b>' kicks in you know how important that discovery of the electric guitar has been, with Scott herself saying "<i>I didn't quite find the sound I was looking for before I started playing electric</i>".<br/><br/>'Honey' is a 5 minute plus amalgamation of <i>EMA</i> like vocals set against some gorgeous guitar work and knowing drums. The lyrics suit the music poignantly, with the not always perfect guitar and vocal delivery matching up with the content of infatuation, jealousy, and betrayal. It is a theme which is repeated and expanded upon during the course of the album. '<b>Jealousy and I</b>' is purposely sparse, with the lyrics of "<i>Jealousy and I, we're two of a kind, and she's all mine</i>" resonating strongly throughout.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>November Baby</b>' is perhaps the most personal and intimate song on the record, so much so you kind of feel like you shouldn't be listening as it sounds like an entirely private affair for Mackenzie herself. But it's this blatant honesty that makes the song all the more endearing, and with the backdrop of a gorgeous sounding guitar throughout the track is a real standout of the album. It's also over 7 minutes long, allowing for plenty of space for everything to be taken in.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>When Winters Over</b>' is a more straight forward rock track, which is fine, but after the delightfully strong opening you are left feeling a little flat. Thankfully '<b>Chains</b>' takes on a different edge entirely, led by an eerie drum machine, Scott's vocals are given full license to roam, and roam they do throughout, with her deep tones penetrating the icy sound scape which is created. It's haunting, truly brilliant stuff.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-VuDmgM3CQ2Y/USKl_4b-III/AAAAAAAAEa8/Tt3wcaUqyDk/s1600/539745_157404721078250_1235360794_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-VuDmgM3CQ2Y/USKl_4b-III/AAAAAAAAEa8/Tt3wcaUqyDk/s320/539745_157404721078250_1235360794_n.jpg" width="213"/></a></div>'<b>Moon and Back</b>' is more of the standard rock stuff, perfectly formed but...yeah. '<b>Don't Run Away Emilie</b>' brings us back to the good stuff, as does '<b>Come To Terms</b>', with both tracks stripped back nature a clear staple for success; letting the vocal/guitar combination stand out and just be lovely. The record finishes with '<b>Waterfall</b>', which is a completely satisfying closing track, featuring soft hooks aplenty, warm ambient bass, and a positive vibe which is at odds with all of what has gone before, obviously.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Captured almost straight to tape '<b>Torres</b>' is an album of often simple and sparse arrangements, something which is incredibly brave for someone of Scott's tender years to bare her thoughts and ideas on such an open platform. It's quite a personal record from start to finish, which when combined with her fairly rangy vocals and retro sounding electric guitar (which is pretty much lush throughout), ultimately leads to a debut album which is bold, authentic, and full of integrity - quite frankly its utterly brilliant.<br/><br/>You can download '<b>Torres</b>' now, or buy the physical version on CD or Vinyl later this month - <a href="http://torrestorrestorres.com/MUSIC" target="_blank"><b>here</b></a>.<br/><br/></div>||
ALBUM: FALL CITY FALL - VICTUS|<div style="text-align: justify;">The fine lines between hardcore punk, post hardcore and metalcore have been obscured within the last decade, predominantly thanks to the attempts by pigeonholed bands to free themselves of categorisation. So, you have hardcore bands positioning themselves as DIY punk rock, post hardcore acts aspiring to lose the ‘post’ (in an attempt to dodge association with the emo-end of the post hardcore spectrum), and metalcore bands refusing the crossover tag in a bid to keep the metal-heads onside. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The most positive outcome from all this musical rejigging is the slew of bands that have just embraced all three subgenres, instead of worrying about what they are and aren’t. Canada’s <b>Fall City Fall</b> are one of these bands. Fall City Fall are: hardcore punk, post hardcore and metalcore. Signed to the legendary but largely inconsistent <b>Victory Records</b>, Fall City Fall are an extreme rock band made of five young members, including not one but two vocalists. ‘<b>Victus</b>’ is their Victory debut, and it’s half an hour of intense, penetrating hardcore, laced with occasional melody, intricate time signatures and bruising breakdowns. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Opener ‘<b>St. James</b>’ serves as a short, slow-burning but brutal introduction, before the <i>Every Time I Die</i> influenced ‘<b>Dissentipede</b>’ kicks in with its vocal swagger and frenetic metalcore riffing. The majority of ‘Victus’ follows a similar, winning formula: fast-paced riffing and punk rock drums effortlessly glide into phases of progressive noodlings or post hardcore melody, before or after a <i>Hatebreed</i>-heavy breakdown. Tracks like ‘<b>Anxiety Attack</b>’ and ‘<b>Shallow Believer</b>’ showcase Fall City Fall’s advanced ability to create angry and technical hardcore music, with the latter featuring some hectic <i>Dillinger Escape Plan</i>-esque noise. Only ‘<b>Many Lives</b>’ offers a brief period of calm, but with its haunting prog guitar lines, the instrumental is more eerie than soothing. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-p746Yh1NoWU/URfmX_1YjUI/AAAAAAAAEY8/5h1a07X2NFs/s1600/577401_491192477580515_45211604_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="238" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-p746Yh1NoWU/URfmX_1YjUI/AAAAAAAAEY8/5h1a07X2NFs/s400/577401_491192477580515_45211604_n.jpg" width="400"/></a>The record highlights come in the form of the impressive closing couplet: ‘<b>Taken</b>’ and ‘<b>Victus</b>’. ‘Taken’ is a slow, controlled moment of chaos, starting with quiet guitars and screamed vocals, progressively getting heavier and fuller, with an escalating, piercing siren sound adding menace in the background. Think a mini version of <i>Converge’s</i> title track from ‘<i>Jane Doe</i>’. The closing title track is an amalgamation of soaring post hardcore and crashing breakdowns, with pained screams and moments of guitar melody, reminiscent of <i>The Bled</i> circa ‘<i>Pass The Flask</i>’. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The dual vocals of <b>Zorn</b> and <b>Pylychaty </b>are visceral and oddly complementary. The low-end growls are heavier than most hardcore vocal performances, while the screamed segments carry a bit of <i>Frank Carter’s</i> impassioned cries during his time fronting <i>Gallows</i> – the sound of unrestrained violence, conveyed all the more convincingly because you can comprehend the lyrics through the noise. Intermittent moments of pained vocal melody come in the form of the now commonplace off-key whine (à la <i>Daryl Palumbo</i>, <i>Keith Buckley,</i> <i>Jason Butler</i>). Fitting, but uninspired. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Nonetheless, Fall City Fall have crafted a near-perfect debut record. Brutal but accessible, it’s crowd-pleasing in their inclusion of headbanging breakdowns, and progressive in their use of innovative mathcore and melody. Personally, I rank ‘Victus’ alongside the modern masterpieces by <i>Converge</i> (‘All We Love We Live Behind’), <i>Letlive.</i> (‘Fake History’) and <i>Vision Of Disorder</i> (‘The Cursed remain Cursed’) for sheer passion, but also for successfully bridging hardcore, post hardcore and metalcore without pretentious mutations of the subgenres’ – um – cores. Absolutely thrilling stuff. // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/fallcityfall" target="_blank"><b>Fall City Fall</b></a> // <a href="http://www.victoryrecords.com/" target="_blank"><b>Victory Records</b></a><br/><br/></div>||
ALBUM: HANDBOOK - TITANOMACHY|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-yFgjwG_06tI/URLbTKg8p_I/AAAAAAAAEVQ/pYoVuzB6MT8/s1600/2647802178-1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-yFgjwG_06tI/URLbTKg8p_I/AAAAAAAAEVQ/pYoVuzB6MT8/s320/2647802178-1.jpg" width="320"/></a></div><b>Handbook</b> (<i>Jake Brown</i>), all the way from York (the old one not the <i>New</i> one) messes with vintage disco, Motown, soul and hip hop hooks, relentless stuttering cut-off and loops, and just the right beats. '<b>Titanomachy</b>' is an album of danceable yet melodically appealing unadulterated remixes; Brown keeps the vintage soul of his samples alive.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">It’s the relentless stuttering loop/cut-off effect of catchy hooks that really gets into your bones. Stand outs include '<b>Feet Feet</b>' with an intensely listenable disco-style flute solo (yes - disco flute) that flickers in a loop/cut-off effect over funk beats and bongos. Irresistible too is '<b>If I</b>' with a looped melodic vocal hook – a laid back soul feel with masterfully layered on subtle and solid beats, this is the sort of track that’s hard to switch off. Opening track '<b>All is Not As it Seems</b>'  hits you with afro sized vocal fanfares and light beats in a 70’s Motown mix up – Brown again manages to create a sound that’s  catchy, danceable, laid back and loud.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>Those Days</b>' plays with old school rap and deeper beats, whilst '<b>Ultimatum</b>' steps away from disco towards the vintage Brooklyn hip hop feel: tasty funk guitar looped at the front of mix and male vocal and rap at the back. It’s a dreamy funk piece with attitude. Brown takes it down for tracks like '<b>Zero</b>' – a sensitively mixed soul track with funk beats and emotional perceptivity - and the atmospheric and quirky '<b>Neurotic</b>' – with stuttering drops into silence and auto-tune disco vocal.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">We hope to catch this guy live soon, but for now head to <a href="http://handbook.bandcamp.com/album/titanomachy" target="_blank"><b>bandcamp</b></a> to check him out and download the album<b>. // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/Handbookah" target="_blank">Handbook</a></b><br/><b> </b> </div>||
ALBUM : WIHT - THE HARROWING OF THE NORTH|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Wphw9q8UnbM/UQbqv-xrvLI/AAAAAAAAETg/Lojph2ytqhM/s1600/300.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="200" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Wphw9q8UnbM/UQbqv-xrvLI/AAAAAAAAETg/Lojph2ytqhM/s200/300.jpg" width="200"/></a></div>Stoner rock has always been the territory of the American yee-haw bands. Across the vast Atlantic however, the correlating British scene struggled to compete. We have grey skies and gloomy post-industrial towns, not sun soaked beaches and expansive deserts - our home grown contemporaries were always going to be different to their cowboy hat wearing cousins.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">So when the now defunct, Leeds based, post-doom-sludge-whateverists <b>Wiht</b> decided to write an instrumental album about <i>William the Conqueror</i> ravaging the North of England, it was always going to be a distinctly English affair. Their final record, ‘<b>The Harrowing of the North</b>’ is a mere two tracks (plus a lengthy bonus track) but is a veritable epic of stoner rock enormity and post rock exploration. Each twist and turn in this capricious monster, from sparkling single notes, wailing guitars and tinkering cymbals to the gigantic, heavy, fuzzed out riffs and booming drums all serve as analogies for William’s marauding armies across the maudlin North, and events leading up to his remorseful deathbed 20 years later.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Wiht might have set themselves a staggering task writing such a record but they manage to convey drama in their music with such aplomb, the entire project is a seemingly effortless success.. ‘The Harrowing...’ is a joy to behold. A swerving, organic beast that you can’t take your ears off, intense and bursting with energy, doom-filled and ominous, it leaves you flabbergasted. This release, in the wake of Wiht’s demise, should be honoured in a fashion akin to the work of any deceased artist of note: with a reverence and awe becoming of a masterpiece, for this record is indeed fitting of such a lofty label. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">‘<b>The Harrowing of the North</b>’ is out 4th February on <a href="http://www.devouterrecords.bigcartel.com/" target="_blank"><b>Devouter Records</b></a>. // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/wihtleeds?fref=ts" target="_blank"><b>Wiht</b></a><br/><br/></div>||
SINGLE: IVORY SEAS - STILL BROODING / MOTHERS TONGUE|<div style="text-align: justify;">Tapping the ambient pop vein, <b>Ivory Seas</b> sew together melodic movement and musical minimalism to create atmospheric tracks ready for the deep icy stills of the British winter. Double A-side with "<b>Mother's Tongue</b>," '<b>Still Brooding</b>' offers a musical chill with a sound truly evocative of the stillness of an icy landscape.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Ivory Seas</b>, who met and got together at Southampton University, compare themselves to popular electronic minimalists such as <i>Antlers</i> and <i>The XX</i>. With their catchy stripped back melodies underlaid by cool ambient sound scattered with sparse yet bold instrumentals the comparison seems apt.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Stripping sound back to stillness without losing the upbeat vibe is what Ivory Seas do well. With clever use of instrumental space and silence - '<b>Still Brooding</b>' has ambient sounds rolled over by clever drum beats courtesy of <i>George Batham</i>, sparse undistorted electronic guitar and wintery lyrics that add to the surreal poetics of the track.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>Mother's Tongue</b>' makes great use of tubular bell/xylophone and deeply ambient backing vocals (<i>Adam Heron</i> and <i>Thomas Walker</i>) that transforms a standard bass/guitar/drum set up into something festive and melodic yet subtle and surreal, a dark watery sound that skilfully ripples the surface just enough to make you smile. // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/ivoryseas" target="_blank"><b>Ivory Seas</b></a> // <a href="http://ivoryseas.bandcamp.com/" target="_blank"><b>Buy 7" White Vinyl</b></a></div>||
