SINGLE: MARIKA HACKMAN - BATH IS BLACK|<div style="text-align: justify;">Ahead of <b>Marika Hackman's</b> debut record in the form of the mini album '<b>That Iron Taste</b>', she recently unveiled an acoustic video for the track '<b>Bath is Black</b>'. It is the first in a series of acoustic videos for each of the albums tracks.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The album, produced by Alt-J's <i>Charlie Andrew</i>, is set to be released through <b>Dirty Hit</b> on 25th February, with Marika supporting the release with some gigs with <i>Ethan Johns</i>, as well as her own headline tour in March.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>Bath Is Black</b>' is wonderfully refreshing in what can sometimes be a stale folk genre. Starting with some delightful guitar finger picking, its Marika's vocals and poignant lyrics which really stand out here. Her voice has a delicate yet somehow knowing quality which belies her tender years, and you can't help but get drawn into her spell of weaving guitar and floating vocals with the song even changing tempo mid track almost seamlessly. The video itself is shot in an old tunnel somewhere in the North of England, and although simple fits the nature of the track really well.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">There are darker undertones throughout this song, a trait which you can't help feel will be repeated on the forthcoming album. That thought not only builds intrigue ahead of the albums release but also further enhances the reputation of someone who is rather quickly building a steadfast fan-base and critical opinion.  <a href="http://www.marikahackman.com/" target="_blank"><b>Marika Hackman</b></a> // <a href="http://www.dirtyhit.co.uk/" target="_blank"><b>Dirty Hit</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div>||
FUTURE SOUNDS OF 2013|<div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;">In last years '<a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/2012/01/future-sounds-of-2012.html" target="_blank"><b>Future Sounds</b></a>' post we tipped <i>Hysterical Injury</i>, <i>Gabrielle Aplin</i>, <i>Daughter</i>, <i>LightGuides</i>, <i>Lucy Rose</i>, and <i>Pale Seas</i>. Most of those acts went on to have a pretty good year, although in the case of Gabrielle Aplin we could never have predicted quite how good! </span><br/><span style="font-size: large;"><br/></span><span style="font-size: large;">This year's list once again features Daughter, not because they didn't have a fantastic 2012, but because their debut album is set to be released this year and we're quite sure it's going to be amazing and propel them onto even bigger and better things, so we're tipping them again! Similarly Keaton Henson appears, despite his first record coming out over 2 years ago, we just felt the spotlight should be shone once again on an artist who is just incredibly talented!</span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/><span style="font-size: large;"><a href="https://www.facebook.com/ohdaughter?ref=ts&amp;fref=ts" target="_blank"><u><b>Daughter</b></u></a> - We've been closely following Elena, Igor, and Remi, since we reviewed their '<a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/2011/12/ep-review-daughter-wild-youth.html" target="_blank"><b>Wild Youth</b></a>' EP back in 2011. Now signed with <span style="font-size: large;">4AD R</span>ecords,<span style="font-size: large;"> t</span>his year will see the release of their debut album which we're ever so excited about, as well as their biggest (sold out) show to date at the <i>Hackney Empire</i>.</span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;"><br/></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;"><a href="https://www.facebook.com/wolfalicemusic?ref=ts&amp;fref=ts" target="_blank"><u><b>Wolf Alice</b></u></a> - Last Summer saw the release of the debut <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/2012/06/ep-review-wolf-alice-wolf-alice.html" target="_blank"><b>self titled EP</b></a> from Wolf Alice, a 3 track soundscape of dreamy folk electronica, which felt really fresh and different. Since then two new singles have emerged, '<b>Leaving You</b>' and this weeks' '<b>Fluffy</b>', which are both more guitar based, but still maintain a clear intent to produce something challenging and interesting.</span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="https://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F63019499" width="100%"></iframe></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;"><br/></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;"><a href="https://www.facebook.com/ninetailsband?ref=ts&amp;fref=ts" target="_blank"><u><b>Ninetails</b></u></a> - Their record '<a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/2012/11/ep-ninetails-slept-and-did-not-sleep.html" target="_blank"><b>Slept and Did Not Sleep</b></a>' was our favourite EP of last year, so it's without doubt that we're looking forward to see what they can come up with in 2013. Catching them live is certainly on our to-do list!</span><br/><br/><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="https://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F62708026" width="100%"></iframe></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;"><br/></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;"><a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Marika-Hackman/113617992037814?ref=ts&amp;fref=ts" target="_blank"><u><b>Marika Hackman</b></u></a> - Miss Hackman has a pretty busy 2012, with singles, live shows, and a stand out covers EP, and now there is the imminent arrival of her debut EP '<b>That Iron Taste</b>', early this year. She's certainly very talented and we're sure her songwriting ability will shine through on the upcoming record.</span><br/><br/><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="https://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F51973541" width="100%"></iframe></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;"><br/></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;"><a href="https://www.facebook.com/keatonhensonfans?ref=ts&amp;fref=ts" target="_blank"><u><b>Keaton Henson</b></u></a> - Keaton Henson has been on our radar since we picked up his debut album '<b>Dear...</b>' back in 2010. Last year saw a re-release of that album, as well as some interesting live shows in museums, and pop up tents around London<span style="font-size: large;">, as well as collaborations<span style="font-size: large;"> and singles.</span></span> Album number two is expected early this year and should propel Keaton onto a much wider audience.</span><br/><br/><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="https://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F61830761" width="100%"></iframe></div>||
THE BLOG SOUND OF 2013 - THE TOP 5|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-aS02wR_puNs/UOWHeVPHg8I/AAAAAAAAEI4/S9wMDTmF450/s1600/blogsound2013+LOGO.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="150" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-aS02wR_puNs/UOWHeVPHg8I/AAAAAAAAEI4/S9wMDTmF450/s200/blogsound2013+LOGO.jpg" width="200"/></a></div>The Blog Sound of 2013 poll is a survey of UK music bloggers to find out what emerging artists they think are best.The votes have been counted, the results are in and the winners can now be revealed.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Congratulations to the winners Haim, who narrowly held off runners up Chvrches by just 1 nomination.<br><br>The 5 artists that received the most votes by the 49 UK music blogs that took part in the poll are:- </br></br></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b><span style="font-size: large;">1st <a href="http://haimtheband.com/" target="_blank">Haim</a></span></b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b><span style="font-size: large;">2nd <a href="https://www.facebook.com/CHVRCHES" target="_blank">Chvrches</a></span></b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b><span style="font-size: large;">3rd= <a href="http://savagesband.com/" target="_blank">Savages</a></span></b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b><span style="font-size: large;">3rd= <a href="http://www.wearepins.co.uk/" target="_blank">Pins</a></span></b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b><span style="font-size: large;">5th <a href="https://www.facebook.com/TheNeighbourhood" target="_blank">The Neighbourhood</a></span></b><br><b><span style="font-size: large;"></span></b><br></br></br></div>||
MUSIC LIBERATION TOP 10 ALBUMS OF 2012|<div style="text-align: justify;">Here's this year's top 10 albums list from <b>Music Liberation</b>. Whilst we didn't quite get to review all of the albums we'd have like to have this year, I feel the records we did get to were all really strong and as a result it was a difficult but wholly enjoyable process of narrowing down the final list you see before you. Hopefully you'll discover something new here you might have missed this year, and at the bottom of the post we also mention those albums we really rated but didn't quite get round to reviewing. 2012 has been a superb year for new music and fortunately for us it only looks like continuing into the new year and beyond. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Thanks for reading, listening, and engaging with Music Liberation this year, we'll be back in 2013 slightly fatter, older, and in some cases greyer, but we'll promise to keep up our desire to review and support the best in new music from across the globe. If you'd like to submit your music to us then please head <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/p/contact.html" target="_blank"><b>here</b></a>, and if you'd like to join the team and write some reviews then go <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/p/writers.html" target="_blank"><b>here</b></a>.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Cheers! x</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><i><b>Jon Sidwell (Editor)</b></i></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"<b>Tall Ships</b> have been on our radar for quite some time now, with us first covering them back in March 2010 with a review of their self titled EP. The trio from Falmouth (now based in Brighton) are signed with the impressive Big Scary Monsters, and Everything Touching is their debut record out as a split release with Blood And Biscuits...<b>Everything Touching</b> is quite possibly one of the best albums you'll hear all year, you just don't know it yet, and for that matter, neither do I, yet. You see this is a complex album which requires several listens to really grasp the depth of ideas this band have put forward over the ten tracks. Some moments are instant, others might take a while longer, but I'm deadly sure that at some point the penny will drop for all...To sum up this album I'll use a vastly overused word - <b>EPIC."</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/>"Just listen to the opening couplet of '<b>Attack On Memory</b>' – and you'll barely recognise them. '<b>No Future / No Past</b>' is slow-burning, moody alternative-rock – not a million miles away from Pixies, with grumbling bass and eerie whining building to an exhilarating last minute in which Baldi screams “no future, no past” repeatedly. Darker, angrier, and a damn lot better than anything Baldi has written before. However, the second track '<b>Wasted Days</b>' is not just the best song of their career, it's the best alternative song of the last few months. At nearly 9 minutes, it's much longer than anything else on the album, but it never feels excessively strung-out. Starting off as a simple garage-punk number with a massive vocal hook, it soon gets stuck into a progressive, vocal-less groove, with bubbling sonic textures and climbing, post-hardcore guitars. It’s sprawling, but the climb is never without precision, and the heavy conclusion features Baldi's best ever vocal performance – barking-then-screaming “<i>I thought I would be more that this</i>” over and over with some mighty, mighty passion. It is <i>huge</i>."</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"It’s a giant of a record; greater than the sum of its rackety and screeching parts, greater even than the crazy trio that fused it all together in a seaside lab full of smoking, bubbling liquids in glass beakers. The twisting, rich guitar riffs dance around horrendously huge staccato rhythms in some kind of punk / dance insanity that that gives zero fucks to what genre it may or may not fit into, whilst echo-drenched vocals occasionally wail out between the ensuing carnage...Look, whatever, it’s stunning. Words are limited, music is infinite and this is one of the most exciting records in years. It it self indulgent?  Yes. Is it inaccessible? Most probably. Is it genius? No doubt. Think <i>Holy Fuck</i>. Think <i>Sleigh Bells</i>. Think <i>World’s End Girlfriend</i>. Think about every electro-punk-rock crossover that you’ve had the displeasure of hearing and then listen to an entire genre being saved by an epic, breath of fresh air that is this album. Inspired, passionate, adventurous and uncompromising, music really doesn't get much better than this."<br/><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Released earlier this year through Bad Panda Records, 'Tokyo Dreamer' is the new album from 17 year old South Korean Sunik Kim. Going under the moniker of Beat Culture, this exceptionally talented young man is already onto album number two, after releasing his debut LP 'Goldenbacked Weaver' in July of last year when he was just 16.His new record, 'Tokyo Dreamer', is a collection of 10 tracks which demonstrates Beat Culture's impeccable knowledge and skills in electronica...The songs that make up <b>Tokyo Dreamer</b> have a great deal of complexity to them and yet somehow <b>Beat Culture</b> seems to make it all sound so simple, and for any audio fan its literally like food for your ears. Taking inspiration from the likes of <i>Burial</i>, <i>James Blake</i>, <i>Fourtet</i>, and <i>Gold Panda</i>, Beat Culture fuses a range of electronic styles such as dub, hip hop, house, and breaks, to create songs which not only get you moving, put you in a really fucking good mood, but can also transport you wherever you'd like to go."</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Dead Wolf Situation is the debut full length album from Bath's Hysterical Injury, a band that should need little introduction to you Music Liberation regulars...My favourite song on the album is '<b>Bitch's Balls</b>' (<i>great title</i>), a track which starts stripped back but is slowly added to with a growing intensity, made up of wild guitars, prominent drums, and far out vocals. Concluding with the monstrous '<b>Rainbow Thunderclap</b>', the '<b>Dead Wolf Situation</b>' experience is one that leaves you feeling part exhausted, part overwhelmed, part enlightened, but in the end wholly satisfied and entirely captivated. As debut albums go its certainly sets the bar high, which will not only challenge those bands around them, but also will surely push the <b>Hysterical Injury</b> onto even greater things in the future. A thought which I hope you'll agree is more than tantalising..."</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div>||
Merry Christmas 2012 : First Aid Kit - Blue Christmas|<div style="text-align: justify;">Merry Christmas from all at <b>Music Liberation</b>! Here's <b>First Aid Kit</b> with this years song, their cover of '<b>Blue Christmas</b>'.</div>||
MUSIC LIBERATION - TOP 10 EP'S OF 2012|<div style="text-align: justify;"><b>"Slept And Did Not Sleep</b> is gloriously experimental but still retains a clear melodic and accessible edge. Comparisons could be drawn with the likes of <i>Wu Lyf</i>, <i>Foals</i>, <i>Late Of The Pier</i>, and <i>Everything Everything</i>, but really <b>Ninetails</b> have their own independent sound. You'll pick up different things on each listen of this record making it a real joy for the ears every time. The potential for this band on a full length release is quite tantalising, as is the impact these songs must have on a live audience."</div><div style="text-align: justify;">"This debut self titled EP from <b>Wolf Alice</b> has a really strong 'feel good' quality to it, with plenty of summery vibes emanating throughout amongst a lush futuristic far away sound-scape . It's perfect for dipping in and out of as the dreamy folky pop songs carry you whether you'd like to go, almost catching you by surprise at how well put together, thought out, and open they are. It's a tantalizing glimpse at the potential this group clearly has, and we look forward to watching them develop over the time to come."</div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Salò’s debut EP is certainly a necessary listen for any fans of the bands name-checked in this review. They have struck an ideal position between math-core experimentalism and melodic post-hardcore – all the while clinging onto a straight-up, hardcore-punk-rock essence, and even splicing some garage-y jangle into the guitars."</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>"Samoans</b> are a three-piece from Cardiff in Wales that have been on my personal radar since 2009-ish when I caught them playing the infamous <i>Clwb Ifor Bach</i> in the Welsh capital. Their style of math-rock inspired guitar music caught my attention straight away and I've been following them ever since. It has been somewhat of a wait then until '<b>Elevated Reflections</b>', their debut EP to come out, however the wait has been more than worth it. The music is melodic, heavy in parts, but also tender too, with the standout track being '<b>Catamaran</b>'."</div><div style="text-align: justify;">"This simple record is nothing if not brave as Wilson’s self-indulgent approach to music may leave some frustrated. These three solemn songs could struggle for mass appeal as they are cyclical in nature, without the salvation of catchy hooks or crowd pleasing string accompaniments. Yet her basic – almost amateur – approach to writing and recording is her strength. In a genre full of cover songs and faux emotion here we are offered sincerity and truth on a plate with what feels like a healthy disregard for popular expectation. It’s refreshing."</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div>||
MUSIC LIBERATION'S SINGLE OF THE YEAR 2012|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-r4jtMBYQH3s/UM-VaxbR_jI/AAAAAAAAEAA/DDLQbya4K6k/s1600/68309_10151207732667973_561565614_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="200" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-r4jtMBYQH3s/UM-VaxbR_jI/AAAAAAAAEAA/DDLQbya4K6k/s200/68309_10151207732667973_561565614_n.jpg" width="195"/></a></div>This years <b>Music Liberation</b> '<b>Single Of The Year</b>' award goes to the ever impressive, hugely hard-working, and insanely talented <b>Crushing Blows</b>, with their single '<b>Hiding Place</b>'.<br/><br/>Released back in February, it was actually a double A side with '<b>You Will Always Be Lonely</b>', and was the build up to the band's latest EP which came out in November of this year. The Derby duo are sure to have lots more exciting projects in store for us in 2013, but for now just sit back and enjoy this incredibly catchy tuuuuune!<br/><br/>To read our original review go <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2012/02/single-review-crushing-blows-hiding.html" target="_blank"><b>here</b></a> // <a href="http://www.crushingblows.co.uk/" target="_blank"><b>Crushing Blows</b></a> // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/Crushingblows" target="_blank"><b>Facebook </b></a></div>||
THE BLOG SOUND OF 2013|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-5g9iuL2-SR0/ULuuSE1_2CI/AAAAAAAAD-Q/AeWJNqWWmuA/s1600/blogsound2013+LOGO.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="240" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-5g9iuL2-SR0/ULuuSE1_2CI/AAAAAAAAD-Q/AeWJNqWWmuA/s320/blogsound2013+LOGO.jpg" width="320"/></a></div><b>Music Liberation</b> is pleased to announce the results of this years <b>Blog Sound Of 2013</b> poll. For those unaware of this interesting snapshot from the blogosphere here's Robin from the <a href="http://www.breakingmorewaves.blogspot.co.uk/" target="_blank"><b>Breaking More Waves</b></a> blog to explain more.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"The Blog Sound Poll was first published in <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/2011/12/blog-sound-of-2012.html" target="_blank">2011</a>. The concept of the poll wasn’t to criticise the established BBC Sound of list, but simply an experiment to see if UK music bloggers could come up with its own list of emerging artists that was more representative of their community and give the artists that were nominated some extra publicity. Indeed the idea was to compliment the BBC list in many ways by providing an alternative to compare and contrast.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Last year’s final long list provided some interesting alternatives to the BBC list; most notably it included Alt-J, this year’s Mercury Prize winners, who didn’t feature on the BBC list at all.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The Blog Sound of 2013 poll has expanded with 49 UK blogs nominating their 5 favourite emerging artists. Just over 170 acts received at least 1 vote. The winning act received votes from around 25% of all bloggers. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The poll was organised by <i>Robin Seamer</i> (<a href="http://www.breakingmorewaves.blogspot.co.uk/" target="_blank"><i>Breaking More Waves</i></a>) and <i>Andy Von Pip</i> (<a href="http://www.thevpme.com/" target="_blank">The Von Pip Express</a>). Each blog was allowed to vote for five acts and the diversity of the nominations was staggering. Based on the evidence of the spread of votes anyone that says that music bloggers are sheep and are all writing about the same artists has got it wrong. However, the results of the poll show that certain artists do have a lot of support and love from a significant portion of UK bloggers and those artists make up the Blog Sound of 2013 list,”.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">So here's the results! (We'll be revealing the top 5 and winner of the <b>Blog Sound of 2013</b> on January 3rd, and we'll also let you know who <b>Music Liberation</b> picked in our customary <b>Future Sounds</b> feature, suffice to say that one of our picks has made the long-list, you can probably guess who!) </div>||
NEW MUSIC: MARIKA HACKMAN|<div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-vv_QxDffovM/ULJ9bZSxvzI/AAAAAAAAD7A/d9o8lAvK0o4/s1600/avatars-000018472088-yrcz0d-crop.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="213" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-vv_QxDffovM/ULJ9bZSxvzI/AAAAAAAAD7A/d9o8lAvK0o4/s320/avatars-000018472088-yrcz0d-crop.jpg" width="320"/></a><b>Marika Hackman</b> is a twenty-year old from London, who earlier this year released her debut material in the shape of a double a-side single '<b><a href="http://soundcloud.com/marika-hackman/marika-hackman-you-come-down" target="_blank"><i>You Come Down</i></a></b>' and '<a href="http://soundcloud.com/marika-hackman/marika-hackman-mountain-spines" target="_blank"><b><i>Mountain Spines</i></b></a>' through Transgressive offshoot <i>Paradyse Records</i>. She recently supported <i>Benjamin Francis Leftwich</i>, and this week she sets out on her own mini headline tour of the UK. Theres also been a 5-track covers EP which has been floating around for a little while, with acts such as <i>Warpaint</i>, <i>Nirvana</i>, <i>Nico</i>, <i>The Knife</i>, and <i>Dusty Springfield</i> all receiving the 'Hackman treatment'. It's fair to say then that she's been a pretty busy lady of late, and with 2013 just round the corner and mentions of further material appearing soon, she's shows no sign of slowing down. But what of her style? </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Well it's folk, but not the happy-go-lucky paint-by-numbers stuff, she has much greater resolve, ideas, and complexity to fit into that bracket. Her voice has great depth, and a dark edge which hints at someone who has done her musical homework and absorbed a wide range of different influences and styles. Returning to the aforementioned EP it is not just the calibre of artists that have been covered, but the approach Marika has taken with it that really shines through, as she brazenly implements her stripped back ideas almost completely transforming the songs into her own material. The cover of '<i>Lithium</i>' by <i>Nirvana</i> in particular stands out, but each track has its own charm. Overall it's a striking listening experience and a tantalising glimpse at what our ears could look forward to next year with the release of new material. We're excited...</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Check out the covers EP and forthcoming headline tour dates<i><b> &gt;&gt;&gt; </b></i> <a href="http://www.marikahackman.com/" target="_blank"><b>www.marikahackman.com</b></a> / <a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Marika-Hackman/113617992037814?ref=ts&amp;fref=ts" target="_blank"><b>Marika Hackman</b></a><br/><br/></div>||
EP: NINETAILS - SLEPT AND DID NOT SLEEP|<div style="text-align: justify;">Signed to <b>Superstar Destroyer Records </b>(<i>awesome name</i>), Liverpools' <b>Ninetails</b> follow up their debut EP '<i>Ghost Ride The Whip</i>' with their new record '<b>Slept And Did Not Sleep</b>'. Straight off I'll let you know I think it's an incredibly ambitious sounding album that arrives with an ever increasing fanfare from the likes of <i>This Is Fake DIY</i> and <i>Clash Magazine</i>. Having already shared stages with <i>Alt-J</i>, <i>Tall Ships</i>, and <i>Errors</i>, Ninetails have certainly built up a strong reputation already despite their short history together as a band.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The 5-track EP kicks with '<b>Maybe We</b>', a defiant opening of rumbling bass and distant guitars which is slowly transformed into a full on rhythmical beast, featuring soaring guitars and transfixing drums, alongside otherworldly vocals. It's a strong opening which sounds really complete and together showing a band clearly in tune with their ideas and intentions. '<b>Body Clock</b>' follows with offbeat drums, intentionally ambiguous vocals, and yet more gorgeous guitars creating those floating hands in the air, slow motion moments. The ending of the song is drawn out, with the band veering off into experimental territory with sound coming and going with various moments of feedback, synths, and drones. For the second track on the record it's a brave decision to stray off the beaten track so early, but it works ever so well.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>Fawdon Fever</b>' is next up, a stunningly groove laden track which never ceases to bore, with the intricate and melodic guitars proving hard to not get consumed by. '<b>Boxed In</b>' is an odd track, being almost devoid of any apparent rhythm or melody, leaving us with distant futuristic bleeps and drones which if nothing else certainly puts you on edge and wondering what on earth is going on. At over 8 minutes in length its not a track which will appeal to all, but if you like to hear different ideas within your musical palette then you may well find something here for you.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Finishing this EP is '<b>Mama Aniseed</b>', a track which seemingly brings together all the elements which have gone before it. There's the experimental electronic moments, melodic guitars, offbeat drums, as well as the first proper introduction to <b>Ed Black's</b> vocals. For me its the guitars which really suck me in with Ninetails, with the delicate riffs and finger picking complimenting the drums perfectly, leading to those brilliant moments of music which just feel completely right, emphatically suiting whatever mood you're in.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Released on December 10th,<b> Slept And Did Not Sleep</b> is gloriously experimental but still retains a clear melodic and accessible edge. Comparisons could be drawn with the likes of <i>Wu Lyf</i>, <i>Foals</i>, <i>Late Of The Pier</i>, and <i>Everything Everything</i>, but really <b>Ninetails</b> have their own independent sound. You'll pick up different things on each listen of this record making it a real joy for the ears every time. The potential for this band on a full length release is quite tantalising, as is the impact these songs must have on a live audience. Speaking of which the band are playing their first London date at the Bull and Gate on November 29th, alongside the Music Liberation endorsed <i>Crushing Blows</i>. We'll see you there!</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://ninetailsband.co.uk/" target="_blank"><b>Ninetails</b></a> // <a href="http://superstardestroyer.bandcamp.com/album/slept-and-did-not-sleep" target="_blank"><b>Stream/Pre-Order EP</b></a> // <a href="http://www.superstardestroyer.co.uk/" target="_blank"><b>Superstar Destroyer Records</b></a><br/><br/></div>||
EP: TO KILL A KING - WORD OF MOUTH|<div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-qXb-MvUf47k/UJwsj6TzRGI/AAAAAAAAD3Y/cNY1NJGlWS8/s1600/391591_502814853079014_1952590182_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-qXb-MvUf47k/UJwsj6TzRGI/AAAAAAAAD3Y/cNY1NJGlWS8/s320/391591_502814853079014_1952590182_n.jpg" width="320"/></a>Hailing from London, <b>To Kill A King</b> may seem a little bit cliché on the surface. They formed at university in Leeds, and they wear the '<i>oh so hip</i>' folk-rock-indie-pop label of so many of their peers - it might be easy for this delightful little band to wash over you altogether. Don't let them, there is a lot more ambition evident here than meets the eye, if latest EP '<b>Word of Mouth</b>' is anything to go by.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">If you heard To Kill A King on the radio, the sharp guitars coupled with <i>Ralph Pelleymounter's</i> croon may evoke a juxtaposition of <i>Editors</i> and <i>Coldplay</i>. However, put this EP through a decent set of headphones on a cold walk home, perhaps thinking of someone special, and it becomes clear that these guys have the potential to go far.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The EP kicks off with '<b>Howling</b>'. Warm, bass filled synth flood the ears - quickly giving way to ambitious multi-instrumentation that will undoubtedly evoke thoughts of <i>The National</i> and delicate vocal harmonies that will pull at the heartstrings. Building to a powerful metallic climax, this really is a great start. Remarkably, To Kill A King ease into top gear on '<b>Funeral</b>', with the intro easily adding shine to any Apple ad, giving way to a tour-de-force in really great song-craft.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Things slow down with '<b>Besides She Said</b>', whereas '<b>Wolves</b>' is a bright, catchy modern indie song with the obligatory anthemic chorus. Momentum builds once again with the brilliant <b>'Rays'</b>, which is rousing indie-pop at it's best, evoking the highlights of big hitters such as <i>Bombay Bicycle Club</i>. Intricate guitars are underpinned with a tight, flexible bass line and a masterful vocal performance from Pelleymounter, ending in a frantic flurry of drums and hi-hat. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Closing track '<b>Let It Die</b>' demonstrates the emotional maturity of the lyrics that run through the heart of this EP. "<i>The saddest part of a broken heart isn't the end so much as the start</i>" will remain with you long after the final chords fade away. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Give me a broken heart any time if it means the start of something this special.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://tokillaking.co.uk/" target="_blank"><b>To Kill A King</b></a> // <a href="http://tokillaking.bandcamp.com/" target="_blank"><b>Buy 'Word Of Mouth' EP</b></a><br/><br/><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="http://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F53087258&amp;show_artwork=true" width="100%"></iframe></div>||
EP: OLILOQUY - THE RED EP|<div style="text-align: justify;">Next up from London’s <b>Sup Peeps Records</b> comes <b>The Red EP</b>, the first of a ‘<i>Three Colours Trilogy</i>’ from <b>Oliloquy</b> (aka <i>CIRCLE</i>), provider of two of the jazziest, funkiest tunes (and a remix) on the label’s introductory two-disc '<a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/2012/10/album-sup-peeps-start-collecting.html" target="_blank"><b>Start Collecting</b></a>' and coming in at only 6 songs long, I decided I would push the boat out and cover each one.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Due for both physical and digital release on Halloween, those expecting the same laidback, jazz-infused vibe from this EP may be disappointed as there is not a trumpet flare or flute flourish to be found. Bare with me though, it’s still worth a listen.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">An ominous, plodding beat sets off intro track ‘<b>Circle’s Theme 1</b>’, building into a gloriously glitch-ridden bass-fest before ‘<b>Borealis</b>’, the EP’s most chilled number, calms things down for a bit. Things get almost cheery on ‘<b>Intelligence</b>’, a good Electronica-inspired track (to my uncouth, Hip Hop-tainted ears, anyway) but it seems a bit too polished which makes it stand out a bit among the murkier EP highlights. The opening of ‘<b>BATS!</b>’ reminded this old drum &amp; bass head of <i>Mampi Swift</i> in his ‘<i>Jaws</i>’ days- never a bad thing. Add a tasty bit of scratching, a familiar-sounding melody that floats in and out and a grimy bassline and the result? A nodding head and thumbs up from me.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">‘<b>Additive</b>’ is a downtempo, almost uneasy listen at first; a droning organ-like sample plus some distorted scratches lead you to think it is another Borealis-esque track. Then the bassline slams in. It is crunchy and chewy and spectacular. I can see this track going down well at whatever the equivalent of a rave is these days (still raves? Someone enlighten me).</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Rounding off this brief extended player in epic form is ‘<b>Invaders From Wherever</b>’, stuffed full of chest-rattling bass, stirring melodies and non-annoying glitch-synth bits (technical term). I’m sure I heard bongo drums just before that first drop too and you can’t not love a tune that features bongos, right? </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">So to sum up, this isn’t one for the acoustic folk lovers. If you like your music bassy, glitchy and covered in synths, you should definitely give <b>The Red EP</b> a listen. Do me one favour when you do though- listen to it on a decent set of speakers, eh? Those tinny little things on your laptop will never do this EP justice. Not in a million years.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Circle-AKA-Oliloquy/183931891637597" target="_blank"><b>Oliloquy</b></a> // <a href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/s/qid=1349435860/ref=sr_grid_albumrank?ie=UTF8&amp;field-keywords=Oliloquy&amp;index=digital-music&amp;rd=1&amp;redirect=true&amp;search-type=ss&amp;sort=albumrank" target="_blank"><b>Pre-Order EP</b></a> // <a href="http://suppeeps.com/" target="_blank"><b>Sup Peeps Records</b></a><br/><br/></div>||
ALBUM: CITIZENS - CTZNS|<div style="text-align: justify;">2012 has been a little quiet on the UK hardcore front. There were some excellent releases last year – with <b>Shapes</b>’ ‘<a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/2011/07/album-review-shapes-monotony-chic.html" target="_blank"><i>Monotony Chic</i></a>’ and <b>The Computers</b>’ ‘<i>This Is The Computers</i>’ becoming two of my favourite noisy albums of the last few years. However, nothing has really stood out this year, at least not to this bored reviewer. However, the debut album from Glasgow trio <b>Citizens</b> – titled ‘<b>CTZNS</b>’ – arrived in my inbox this week, and all of a sudden I was bored no longer.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Having released two well-received EPs – including the formidable ‘<b>Try Harder</b>’ EP – and built up a rather respectable live reputation, one might have expected Citizens to take their time constructing their first full length. WRONG. ‘<b>CTZNS</b>’ was recorded in a single day, live! Yet, the production quality is remarkably fine, especially considering the erratic and heavy nature of the music. For this we must surely commend the engineer and studio (<i>Bruce Rintoul</i> and <i>Lofi Studio</i>, Glasgow), as well as the impressive tightness of the trio’s instrumentation.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Citizens make hectic, progressive hardcore – with experimental time signatures, frantic riffing, emotive and throaty vocals, and punk rock pacing. There are snippets of post hardcore in the more melodic or jangly segments of ‘CTZNS’, such as the first half of ‘<b>Heavy Breather</b>’ (before the punishing, sludgy riff and earthy vocals of the final stretch) or the mid section of the sprawling epic that is closer ‘<b>Distance Blues</b>’.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">However, for the most part, this is aggressive hardcore punk with math-rock noodlings. Take the 49 second track ‘<b>New Punks</b>’, which despite its short, sharp punk structure, still manages to fit in some jumpy off-kilter guitars. Some of <i>Craig McIntyre’s</i> guitar work is thrilling, such as on the instrumental ‘<b>Hats Off To Phil Differ</b>’ and the glorious, slow burning opener ‘<b>Habitual Smoker Blues</b>’. Previous single ‘<b>Try Harder</b>’ (from the EP of the same name) reappears here, and is perhaps the track that best showcases what Citizens are all about – slow, chunky riffs and ear-splitting screams that evolve into stabbing, proggy playfulness, bouncing alongside<i> Owen Batchelor’s</i> grumbling bass, before a heavy riff mean enough to slay and bury an emo kid dominates the rest of the song. It’s all very <i>Pulled Apart By Horses</i> (before they moved into more alt-rock territory). </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The fact that ‘<b>Woollen Mammoth</b>’ is the album highlight is unmistakable. The quick-fire, stop-start riffing and monumental shifts in structure encapsulate all the best trademarks of post hardcore, progressive hardcore, mathcore – hell, it’s HARDCORE to its…core. Citizens are the best new UK (post) (progressive) hardcore outfit to emerge in 2012, hands down. Their music manages to be intelligent yet accessible, and as heavy as a blissful head-butt in a punk rock mosh pit. SUPPORT! <b> </b><br/><br/><a href="https://www.facebook.com/citizenshcband" target="_blank"><b>Citizens</b></a> // <a href="http://citizens.bandcamp.com/album/ctzns" target="_blank"><b>Buy 'CTZNS'</b></a> / You can catch Citizens on their European tour throughout October/November, get involved!</div>||
ALBUM: SUP PEEPS - START COLLECTING|<div style="text-align: justify;">London based <b>Sup Peeps Records</b> may not be a familiar name for most- it wasn’t to me anyway, but <b>'Start Collecting'</b>, the first compilation from this enigmatic label is a jazzy, funky, hip hop-ified two-disc rollercoaster that is well worth checking out.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">If you ask me, when the compilation gets its jazz-funk on is when it is at its strongest. Album opener <b>'Asa715'</b> by <b>Four Leaf Sound</b> and '<b>CIRCLE</b>' aka <b>Oliloquy’s</b> two contributions (<b>'I’ll Drive the Band'</b> and <b>'The Subject Is…'</b>) set the bar high and if you don’t find yourself nodding along to '<b>Sepia Sky</b>' by <b>OdjBox</b>, I simply don’t think we could ever be friends.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Disc two starts strong too. There’s something hypnotic about the bells and vocal sample in <b>Trig’s</b> <b>'Kibou no Kiseki (Track of Hope)'</b> and <b>Jill Peacock</b> shows us on '<b>Up in the Air</b>' that she has a pretty awesome voice.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">A couple of tracks, '<b>Got to Get On Now</b>' by <b>Yuki Kanesaka</b> and '<b>Twist off Cap</b>' by <b>Big Hell</b> feature beats that sound a bit too much like the classic two-step beat of UK Garage for my taste but may conjure nostalgic vibes for those of a similar vintage to me (I was always more of a drum &amp; bass fan myself). They stick out a little among the more laid back tracks but may offer a pleasant change of gears if the jazz gets a bit much for you. The rapper on '<b>Got to Get On Now</b>' will never set the Hip Hop on fire either…</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">If you’re a fan of UK Hip Hop, look up <b>Boodacon</b>. His performance on DJ Buzzword’s <b>Small Town Pleasures</b> is (and I’m guessing he’ll hate this comparison if he reads this) reminiscent of <i>Mike Skinner</i>… If Mike Skinner knew how to flow ON a beat instead of around it, although he does veer into ‘talking over the beat’ territory. If the original of Hot Donkey’s Disregard is as funky as Ali Jameson’s remix, then I’m looking them up when I finish this review. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">All in all, I’d say <b>Stay Collecting</b> is well worth a listen, or even worth dusting off your wallet. If this is a taste of things to come from <b>Sup Peeps</b>, I recommend making a note of the name and the talented bunch that album A&amp;R <i>Jay Kenny</i> got together.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://suppeeps.com/" target="_blank"><b>Sup Peeps Records</b></a> // <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RPGcscCIiwk&amp;feature=channel_video_title" target="_blank"><b>Album Trailer</b></a> // <a href="http://soundcloud.com/sup-peeps-records/sets/sup-peeps-start-collecting" target="_blank"><b>Stream/Buy 'Start Collecting'</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div>||
ALBUM: TALL SHIPS - EVERYTHING TOUCHING|<div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Tall Ships</b> have been on our radar for quite some time now, with us first covering them back in March 2010 with a review of their <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.co.uk/2010/03/ep-review-tall-ships-tall-ships.html" target="_blank"><b>self titled EP</b></a>. The trio from Falmouth (now based in Brighton) are signed with the impressive <b>Big Scary Monsters</b>, and <b>Everything Touching</b> is their debut record out next week on October 8th as a split release with <b>Blood And Biscuits</b>.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The album begins with '<b>T=O</b>', a sumptuous half instrumental <i>Mogwai</i> inspired track which sets the bar ever so high. Vocalist <b>Ric Phethean</b> enters halfway through, but it is the guitars that really shine bright. Launching straight into '<b>Best Ever</b>', the band continue their impressive early <i>Foals-esq</i> mathrock, with once again those guitars really standing out. It's heavy, but also it's not, in a weird way, as the melodic rhythmic nature of the music carries you effortlessly along. Things are slowed a tad for third track '<b>Phosopherence</b>', with Plethean's vocals given more of the limelight. It's a solid track, if nothing spectacular especially after the opening first two tracks. '<b>Oscar</b>' starts in a similar fashion to the previous song, but after a slow start things get ramped up for an emphatic guitars driven ending (<i>ED: yes more guitars!</i>).<br/><br/>'<b>Ode To Ancestors</b>' is simply beautiful, vocally and musically, with the sparseness in the track enhancing everything. Things get moving halfway through and the familiar pattern of group vocals and big guitars takes us through to the end. It builds and builds until you are forced to take notice, but actually it really works well and its a pleasure to let the band take over your mind. The one track I struggle with on this album is '<a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Wa4Y8RO590A" target="_blank"><b>Gallop</b></a>', purely because it reminds me of <i>The Vaccines</i>, with the vocals, and the drumming in particular reminding me of that bloody band (<i>ED: let it go Jon, it was a long time ago...</i>). Did I mention that also happens to be the latest single from the record?</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Moving swiftly on, '<b>Idolatry</b>' sounds gigantic, with the band somehow creating even more space and variety in their music. During the six minutes of the track heart strings are tugged, heads are rocked, feet are tapped, and your mind will definitely be taken someplace else. It's a different track to others on the album, with the band moving away from their trusted guitar riffs and being more experimental, and it works, really well. An entire album of tracks just like that would go down very well (<i>ED: hint, hint</i>). '<b>Books</b>' is the thinking mans' song, lyrics about time being precious, interspersed with soaring guitars and big drums. Nice. Final track '<b>Murmurations</b>' is an epic nine-minuter, growing from a distance beat and lone guitar into a full on rhythmic monster with keys, guitars, drums, and vocals all combining to leave a song which is just a joy to listen to again and again.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Everything Touching</b> is quite possibly one of the best albums you'll hear all year, you just don't know it yet, and for that matter, neither do I, yet. You see this is a complex album which requires several listens to really grasp the depth of ideas this band have put forward over the ten tracks. Some moments are instant, others might take a while longer, but I'm deadly sure that at some point the penny will drop for all, with the album sure to feature in many top 10's come the end of the year. To sum up this album I'll use a vastly overused word - <b>EPIC.</b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://tallshipsband.bigcartel.com/product/everything-touching-cd-album" target="_blank"><b>Pre-Order/Buy 'Everything Touching</b></a>' // <a href="http://www.wearetallships.co.uk/" target="_blank"><b>Tall Ships</b></a> // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/bigscarymonsters?ref=ts&amp;fref=ts" target="_blank"><b>Big Scary Monsters</b></a> / <a href="https://www.facebook.com/bloodandbiscuits?ref=ts&amp;fref=ts" target="_blank"><b>Blood And Biscuits</b></a></div>||
ALBUM: NEGATIVE PEGASUS - LOOMING|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Z2GXf4cBGbM/UF8Hkrzsz-I/AAAAAAAADyM/2VPSniRRZTw/s1600/e1807fa67a59336e4f84c550952597e0efd5a7c2.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Z2GXf4cBGbM/UF8Hkrzsz-I/AAAAAAAADyM/2VPSniRRZTw/s320/e1807fa67a59336e4f84c550952597e0efd5a7c2.jpg" width="320"/></a></div><b>Negative Pegasus</b>, or “<i>Neg Peg</i>” as fans should, and most probably are, calling them are three mad scientists from Brighton, mixing together the phatest, scariest beats you’ll hear this side of the English channel. And like the Frankensteinian monster it is, debut album ‘<b>Looming</b>’ wanders around, clumsy and aimless, smashing the shit out of anything in its path; mostly, your ears.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">It’s a giant of a record; greater than the sum of its rackety and screeching parts, greater even than the crazy trio that fused it all together in a seaside lab full of smoking, bubbling liquids in glass beakers. The twisting, rich guitar riffs dance around horrendously huge staccato rhythms in some kind of punk / dance insanity that that gives zero fucks to what genre it may or may not fit into, whilst echo-drenched vocals occasionally wail out between the ensuing carnage. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Forget hyperbole, this record is genius. Here are some adjectives that are literally being extracted from my head upon listening: Fuck off tonal slabs / Monolithic chunks of analogue blasts / Raw and primal grooves / Rhythmic sucker-punches of distortion / Sonic angularities / Guttural guitar barks / Psychedelic vocal wails / Swaggering stuttery monstrosities / Gargantuan tanks of noise / Red raw strips of vulgar howls / Propulsive instrumentals / Unadulterated guitar riffage / Screaming seas of feedback / Manic explosions of sound / spiky and haunting guitar echos / growling rumbles of square shaped frequencies / ominous and dronal pomposities… </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-j6GF1UnUeGY/UF8IrpJW9VI/AAAAAAAADyU/lkse6MdsMss/s1600/7106268641_a7897a986a_z.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="200" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-j6GF1UnUeGY/UF8IrpJW9VI/AAAAAAAADyU/lkse6MdsMss/s200/7106268641_a7897a986a_z.jpg" width="160"/></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/>Look, whatever, it’s stunning. Words are limited, music is infinite and this is one of the most exciting records in years. It it self indulgent?  Yes. Is it inaccessible? Most probably. Is it genius? No doubt. Think <i>Holy Fuck</i>. Think <i>Sleigh Bells</i>. Think <i>World’s End Girlfriend</i>. Think about every electro-punk-rock crossover that you’ve had the displeasure of hearing and then listen to an entire genre being saved by an epic, breath of fresh air that is this album. Inspired, passionate, adventurous and uncompromising, music really doesn't get much better than this. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The aptly named ‘<b>Looming</b>’ will be released by <b>Small Town America</b>, home of some of the best guitar bands of recent years, on 24th September 2012. It is highly advised you buy it.<br/><br/><b><a href="http://www.independentmusic.com/releases/negative-pegasus-looming" target="_blank">Buy Album</a></b> / <b><a href="https://www.facebook.com/negativepegasus" target="_blank">Negative Pegasus</a></b> / <b><a href="http://www.smalltownamerica.co.uk/" target="_blank">Small Town America</a></b><br/><br/></div>||
SINGLE: LAURA WELSH - CALL TO ARMS / HOLLOW DRUM|<div style="text-align: justify;">If <b>Laura Welsh</b> turned our heads earlier this year with the introduction of her debut track '<b>Ghosts</b>', then she's making us do cartwheels now with not one but two brand new tracks, '<b>Call To Arms</b>', and '<b>Hollow Drum</b>'.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Both tracks show off her remarkable voice, which really does need to be heard, any words I could write will never do it justice. While the music itself is sparse but perfectly arranged. Little is known about her at this stage, but if the quality of tracks released so far is anything to go by then that won't last for long.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://laurawelsh.tumblr.com/" target="_blank"><b>Laura Welsh</b></a> / <a href="http://soundcloud.com/laurawelsh" target="_blank"><b>Soundcloud</b></a> / <a href="https://www.facebook.com/laurawelshofficial" target="_blank"><b>Facebook</b></a> / <a href="https://twitter.com/_laurawelsh" target="_blank"><b>Twitter</b></a></div>||
EP: CARA MITCHELL - HAVE YOU EVER WONDERED|<div style="text-align: justify;">At just 16 years of age, Scottish lass <b>Cara Mitchell </b>could be forgiven for filling her young mind with many different thoughts, from aspirations for the future, ideas of discovery, or just deciding whether or not it's possible to fit another episode of '<i>Hollyoaks</i>' into a busy night of television viewing (<i>ED: Young people still watch Hollyoaks right?</i>). And whilst she may indeed spend her time contemplating such things, she has also managed to fit into her schedule the writing and recording of her debut EP '<b>Have You Ever Wondered</b>'.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Released through <b>AGP</b> on September 23rd, the four-track record begins with the title track '<b>Have You Ever Wondered</b>', a truly simple yet glorious folk song, which introduces Cara's delicate vocals and her obvious ear for space within her music. '<b>Passing Sun</b>' furthers the strength of her infectious vocals, but it is the combination of her excellent hard/soft acoustic guitar which enhances the poignancy of the lyrics she's singing. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-lSrZtMQ7T6o/UFJI0oPUocI/AAAAAAAADvE/TRe4QuXh5UA/s1600/Cara+Trend+2+(FILEminimizer).jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="135" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-lSrZtMQ7T6o/UFJI0oPUocI/AAAAAAAADvE/TRe4QuXh5UA/s200/Cara+Trend+2+(FILEminimizer).jpg" width="200"/></a> </div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>Next October</b>' shows a greater depth to her voice, which should only get better as she gets older, albeit she might lose that quirky daintiness which comes from being so young. The EP closes with '<b>Little Birdies</b>', another perfectly formed track which introduces yet another style of singing from Cara, which is more jaunty and direct helping to put you in the moment, where if you close your eyes you really could imagine walking through a forest, with the sun shining, and the birds singing. Bliss.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Cara Mitchell's</b> debut EP '<b>Have You Ever Wondered</b>' does more than just show much promise, it actually delivers straight off the bat. Never has the '<i>maturity beyond her years</i>' tag appeared more deservedly on  <b>Music Liberation</b>. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">You can catch Cara supporting <i>Esperi</i> during their UK tour during September/October. // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/CaraMitchellMusic/app_139114646178872" target="_blank"><b>Pre-Order EP</b></a> // <a href="http://www.caramitchell.net/" target="_blank"><b>Cara Mitchell</b></a></div>||
SINGLE REVIEW: DEAD WOLF CLUB - RADAR|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-tmxDdsc5Yqc/TzQ1yJDX-kI/AAAAAAAADaM/rAsY8RFbFFE/s1600/dwci.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="240" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-tmxDdsc5Yqc/TzQ1yJDX-kI/AAAAAAAADaM/rAsY8RFbFFE/s320/dwci.jpg" width="320"/></a></div><b>Dead Wolf Club</b> are pretty energetic. Single ‘<b>Radar</b>’ starts with a lone guitar line that sounds like the song is going to explode into a raging flurry of head-nodding, chaotic rhythms and riffs that will make you want to lose track of space and time in a dingy indie club somewhere off <i>Charing Cross Road</i> as you slowly inhale tequila and cover yourself in a thin balm of stale beer and sickly sweat on a packed dance floor.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">It’s unfortunate then that such a hypnotic climax seems just out of reach for the ambitious teenage foursome. When ‘Radar’ does kick in, it’s less explosive than expected and instead is a brooding ride that tips its hat firmly at <i>Interpol</i>. Vocals are angsty wails that sit over minor key progressions whilst propulsive drums stimulate the snare-to-neck nerve endings a treat. Proceedings are rudely interrupted however in the form of a stuttering bridge that means that when we get to the soaring chorus, intensity is lost. A minor nag perhaps but enough to break the spell, put down the tequila and think about work tomorrow.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">In all honesty, the intro of ‘Radar’ might be ‘<i>Last Night</i>’ by <i>The Stokes</i>, the middle Interpol and the end stolen from ‘<i>Banquet</i>’ by <i>Bloc Party</i> but so what? Dead Wolf Club make a bold enough musical statement here that this song has a charm of its own. The band call their music “<i>dark punk</i>” but this single is a no nonsense slice of indie rock nostalgia. Couple this with an apparent reputation for vitriolic live shows and smashed guitars and it starts to become impossible to not like this promising bunch.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Dead Wolf Club</b> are smashing guitars and being vitriolic all over the UK with a tour to celebrate the release of their <a href="http://www.deadwolfclub.com/">debut self titled album</a>, which came out earlier this month through <a href="http://www.scenenotherd.org/"><b>Scene Not Herd</b></a>. // <a href="http://www.deadwolfclub.com/"><b>DEAD WOLF CLUB</b></a></div>||
LIVE REVIEW : Lucy Rose at the Jazz Cafe (Camden, London, 4th February 2012)|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-1ZuMbdrGE2M/TzGbRXDBEwI/AAAAAAAADZ8/Vsgpi1IuBqU/s1600/182625_183949488308402_150865674950117_370582_1783502_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="213" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-1ZuMbdrGE2M/TzGbRXDBEwI/AAAAAAAADZ8/Vsgpi1IuBqU/s320/182625_183949488308402_150865674950117_370582_1783502_n.jpg" width="320"/></a></div>Having made the <b>Music Liberation</b> '<a href="http://www.musicliberation.blogspot.com/2012/01/future-sounds-of-2012.html">Future Sounds of 2012</a>' list,<b> Lucy Rose</b> was a name we were always going to look out for during the year ahead. So when the opportunity came about to catch her playing her largest gig to date at the <b>Jazz Cafe</b> in <b>Camden</b>, we jumped at the chance. Not even the '<i>heavy onslaught</i>' of snow which decided to engulf the capital the moment we set off could dampen the spirits and anticipation of checking out the young lady from Warwickshire, who in a relatively short period of time has gone from being that girl who joins <i>Bombay Bicycle Club</i> from time to time, to being recognised in her own right as an artist with much integrity and a clear desire and confidence to put out her own ideas.<br/><br/>Taking to the stage with a collection of musicians who intermittently appear from one song to the next, Lucy gets things going with '<b>Middle Of The Bed</b>', a track we <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/11/ep-review-lucy-rose-middle-of-bed.html"><b>reviewed last November</b></a>, and a track which neatly demonstrates how infectious her music is. I suppose you could put her in the 'acoustic' bracket, however there is a growing sense of intensity that builds within her songs, emanating from the different instruments which surround Lucy's own fine guitar playing. Whilst her vocals steal the headlines, both from a songwriting perspective and sonically, the music behind her is also of such a standard and complexity that the combination is really quite mesmerising. With the Jazz Cafe completely sold out (and apparently over sold with some ticket holders turned away at the door) the atmosphere inside was for want of a better word, <i>special</i>.<br/><br/><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-TWJSi2OA_fE/Ty5lRvYIcaI/AAAAAAAADZU/hlG_mmZYKIE/s1600/132843978350877999.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="200" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-TWJSi2OA_fE/Ty5lRvYIcaI/AAAAAAAADZU/hlG_mmZYKIE/s200/132843978350877999.jpg" width="158"/></a>Lucy seemed to grow with confidence as each song went by, not surprising with this being her biggest show to date, and a gig at which she thought '<i>only 20 people</i>' would show up at! Mixing some older songs with new, highlights included '<b>Gamble</b>' (for the record Lucy confirmed she does NOT have a problem with gambling), '<b>Rocking Newbie</b>' (a working title for a song which had its debut live airing), and '<b>Don't You Worry</b>' (a track which you might have heard during the latest episode of <i>Skins</i>, if you're like me and still watch it that is). My favourite track of the night would have to be '<b>Shiver</b>', a beautifully simple song that really puts the spotlight on Lucy's ethereal vocals which draw you in and capture your attention, in much the same way as her contemporaries of the moment <b>Daughter</b>, <b>Gabrielle Aplin</b>, and <b>Kyla La Grange</b>.<br/><br/><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-08HG2BGnTO8/Ty5kEpYYi3I/AAAAAAAADZM/r2la-A0YFKM/s1600/132843978350877.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="161" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-08HG2BGnTO8/Ty5kEpYYi3I/AAAAAAAADZM/r2la-A0YFKM/s200/132843978350877.jpg" width="200"/></a>All too soon the show is over, finishing with her latest single '<b>Red Face</b>', however we do get treated to what Lucy says is her first ever encore, with the time stopping '<b>First</b>' capturing everyones attention one last time. To emphasise how enthralling the gig was one member of the crowd even asked Lucy to play 'Middle Of The Bed' to which she replied "<i>that is a classic but I've already played that one!</i>" This is actually another side to Lucy which developed during the show, her ability to communicate with the crowd on a level that was quite endearing, with her strong stage presence being quite refreshing for someone so young. So all in all a superb gig, and the subsequent battle getting home with the snow and apparent inability of the tube network to deal with it seemed to matter little after witnessing such an enthralling performance.<br/><br/>With her debut album currently being recorded and a trip to America supporting Bombay Bicycle Club to look forward to, Lucy Rose has a very exciting year ahead of her, and we at Music Liberation are certainly looking forward to hearing and watching more of her in the months to come.<br/><br/><a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Lucy-Rose/150865674950117?sk=wall"><b>Lucy Rose</b></a> // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/jazzcafecamden"><b>The Jazz Cafe</b></a><b>  // <a href="http://lucyrose.net/">LucyRose.Net</a> </b><i>(excellent fansite for Lucy)</i><b><br/></b></div>||

ALBUM REVIEW: CLOUD NOTHINGS - ATTACK ON MEMORY|<div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Cloud Nothings</b> <i>used</i> to be mediocre. Cloud Nothings <i>used</i> to be forgettable. Cloud Nothings <i>used</i> to be a solo-project. Of their show supporting <i>Crocodiles</i> at the <i>Camden Barfly</i>, this time last year, I referred to their “<i>brand of jangly pop-punk</i>” as “<i>upbeat and energetic but exceptionally bland and generic</i>”. However, Cloud Nothings' new record – '<b>Attack On Memory</b>' – is the sound of a band revitalised. It is the sound of a band emerging as <i>vital</i>.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Ohio natives Cloud Nothings began as the vehicle for a lone <b>Dylan Baldi</b>, the frontman and principle songwriter who played all the instruments on their first two albums – '<b>Turning On</b>' and the self-titled follow-up. The inadequacies of those first two flat records were hidden behind infectious melodies, with Baldi pushing for bright, DIY pop-punk (with the emphasis on<i> pop</i>) but failing to pen enough memorable guitar or drum parts. Basically, imagine a boring <i>Mazes</i> with irritating vocals. 'Attack On Memory' is the first album to be recorded as a full band, and as a result it sounds much...<i>fuller</i>. This may also have a little something to do with getting in <b>Steve Albini</b> to man the recording process (that guy who did <b>Pixies' 'Surfer Rosa'</b>, <i>THAT GUY WHO DID <b>NIRVANA'S 'IN UTERO</b>'</i>). Although Baldi has stated that all Alibini did during the sessions was play on Facebook, and blog about food (hmmmm?!).</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Hk4O1CsfrTU/TynHkzbPbNI/AAAAAAAADY8/SSEJubFtxfg/s1600/120201-cloud-nothings.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Hk4O1CsfrTU/TynHkzbPbNI/AAAAAAAADY8/SSEJubFtxfg/s1600/120201-cloud-nothings.png"/></a>So, how have Cloud Nothings changed? Just listen to the opening couplet of '<b>Attack On Memory</b>' – and you'll barely recognise them. '<b>No Future / No Past</b>' is slow-burning, moody alternative-rock – not a million miles away from Pixies, with grumbling bass and eerie whining building to an exhilarating last minute in which Baldi screams “no future, no past” repeatedly. Darker, angrier, and a damn lot better than anything Baldi has written before. However, the second track '<b>Wasted Days</b>' is not just the best song of their career, it's the best alternative song of the last few months. At nearly 9 minutes, it's much longer than anything else on the album, but it never feels excessively strung-out. Starting off as a simple garage-punk number with a massive vocal hook, it soon gets stuck into a progressive, vocal-less groove, with bubbling sonic textures and climbing, post-hardcore guitars. It’s sprawling, but the climb is never without precision, and the heavy conclusion features Baldi's best ever vocal performance – barking-then-screaming “<i>I thought I would be more that this</i>” over and over with some mighty, mighty passion. It is <i>huge</i>.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Too huge, in fact, as the record never really matches those impeccable heights. The simplistic, pop-punk numbers sound ten times tighter (and three times heavier) than pre-album three, with '<b>Cut You</b>' and single '<b>Stay Useless</b>' featuring Cloud Nothings' best ever pop-melodies, and '<b>Fall In</b>' and '<b>Our Plans</b>' incorporating an intelligent emo sensibility (like <i>Drive Thru's The Early November</i>, or <i>Deep Elm's</i> roster). These songs are good, great even, but one can't help wishing that Baldi had allowed the band to flesh out these tunes, in the same way they beat up 'Wasted Days' to perfection. You see, the only major gripe I have with Cloud Nothings is Baldi's voice. He basically sounds like a couple of teeny, tiny blocked nostrils, so his voice isn't particularly well suited to the melodic pop-punk that he seems intent on producing. His voice is much better suited to post-hardcore whines, barks and screams, or the groaning grunge of '<b>No Sentiment</b>' – a brooding mid-paced number with splashy drums and distorted guitar work. The most exciting track actually comes in the form of an instrumental: '<b>Separation</b>'. This ferocious punk-rock song is built around an insanely catchy, spiky guitar riff (catchier than any vocal hook on the album), and contains urgent, quick-fire drums, with snare, snare, and SNARE all over the place.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">If it sounds like I found the album disappointing, then I have misled you. There is real quality to the record as a whole, with the vocals, drums and guitar parts having been considerably improved. The production is spot on, and the song structures are given enough room to breathe sufficiently, effortlessly, yet managing to retain Baldi's sense of sharpness. But just listen to '<b>Wasted Days</b>' and think to yourself: what if <b>Cloud Nothings</b> produced a whole album of 'Wasted Days''...WHAT IF!? Nonetheless, this is essential listening for fans of any sort of melodic punk (post, pop, garage, etc).</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'ATTACK ON MEMORY' IS RELEASED 6TH FEBRUARY THROUGH <a href="http://shop.wichita-recordings.com/DigitalProduct.aspx?rid=379&amp;fid=12&amp;brid=5"><b>WICHITA</b></a> // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/cloudnothings?sk=wall"><b>CLOUD NOTHINGS</b></a></div>||
New Music : The Cast Of Cheers|<div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Ir112VJFXI4/Tx881HX6HKI/AAAAAAAADYo/IDaHWO8iKE8/s1600/373396_175599531922_221365877_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Ir112VJFXI4/Tx881HX6HKI/AAAAAAAADYo/IDaHWO8iKE8/s1600/373396_175599531922_221365877_n.jpg"/></a>With a slightly odd and potentially unfavourable name, <b>The Cast Of Cheers</b> make up for it somewhat with their brilliant debut single '<b>Family</b>', which will be released through <b>School Boy Error</b> / <b>Cooperative Music</b> on February 20th. It's jaunty, mathy, and unquestionably fun, and the video is splendid too. We are very much looking forward to keeping an eye on these guys over the forthcoming months. You can catch them playing alongside <b>Theme Park</b> (who you might recall from making the top 5 of <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2012/01/blog-sound-of-2012-top-5.html"><i>The Blog Sound of 2012</i></a>) during February and March.<br/><br/><span style="font-size: x-small;"><a href="http://www.thecastofcheers.com/"><b>The Cast Of Cheers</b></a> <b></b> <a href="http://www.facebook.com/thecastofcheers?sk=wall"><b>Facebook</b></a> <b></b> <a href="http://www.twitter.com/thecastofcheers"><b>Twitter</b></a></span></div>||
Future Sounds of 2012|<div style="text-align: justify;">Better late than never, here is this years 'Future Sounds' post, which contains a collection of artists we can't wait to hear new material from this year.<br/><br/><span style="font-size: large;"><u><b>Hysterical Injury</b></u></span> <span style="font-size: x-small;">// <a href="http://www.facebook.com/thehystericalinjury"><b>Facebook</b></a> / <a href="http://twitter.com/hiband"><b>Twitter</b></a></span><br/>Ever since we put forward Hysterical Injury for the Emerging Talent Stage for last year's Glastonbury, we've told anyone that will listen just how great they are. At the back end of last year that even included Tom Robinson, who played the band on his <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/blogs/nowplaying/2011/12/6music2012---what-the-bloggers.shtml">BBC 6Music show</a> as we told him he had to (as did Tiffany from <a href="http://www.drunkenwerewolf.com/"><b>Drunken Werewolf</b></a>). 2012 see's the band release their debut LP '<b>Dead Wolf Situation</b>', and we can tell you now, its brilliant!</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="http://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F34200014&amp;show_artwork=true" width="100%"></iframe><br/><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;"><u><b>Gabrielle Aplin</b></u> </span><span style="font-size: x-small;">//</span> <span style="font-size: x-small;"><a href="http://www.facebook.com/GABRIELLEAPLINOFFICIAL"><b>Facebook</b></a> / <a href="http://www.twitter.com/gabrielleaplin"><b>Twitter</b></a></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">We first discovered Bath's <b>Gabrielle Aplin</b> back in late <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2010/08/interview-gabrielle-aplin.html">2010</a>, and since then we've kept a keen eye on her development. Earlier this month she released her latest EP, '<b>Home</b>', which is her strongest work to date, and has left us eagerly awaiting a future full length album hopefully later this year. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="http://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F29207447&amp;show_artwork=true"
