;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;p&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;br&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;br&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;DD&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;/p&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;/p&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;/p&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;/p&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;/p&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;/p&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;/p&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;/p&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;/p&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;/p&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;lt;/p&amp;amp;amp;amp;amp;gt;&amp;lt;/p&amp;gt;</iframe></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;"><u><b>Daughter</b></u></span> // <a href="http://www.facebook.com/ohdaughter"><b>Facebook</b></a> / <a href="http://www.twitter.com/ohdaughter"><b>Twitter</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Having waxed lyrical about <b>Daughter's</b> 2nd EP at the end of last year (<a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/12/ep-review-daughter-wild-youth.html"><b>The Wild Youth</b></a>), its fair to say we are more than a little bit interested to hear what Elena has in store for us in 2012. Not to mention checking her out again at one of her gigs, which last year were truly something special.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="http://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F26923300&amp;show_artwork=true" width="100%"></iframe></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;"><u><b>LightGuides</b></u></span> <span style="font-size: x-small;">// <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/LightGuides/235016908020"><b>Facebook</b></a> / <a href="http://twitter.com/lightguides"><b>Twitter</b></a></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Having put out one of our favourite debut EP's of last year (<a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/10/ep-review-lightguides-samba-samba-samba.html"><b>Samba Samba Samba</b></a>), and belonging to the <a href="http://alcopop.wordpress.com/shop/">Alcopop! Records</a> stable, Glasgow's <b>LightGuides</b> are a band we're looking forward to learning more about as we chart their seemingly unstoppable progress during the coming year.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="http://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F21345855&amp;show_artwork=true" width="100%"></iframe></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: large;"><u><b>Lucy Rose</b></u></span> <span style="font-size: x-small;">// <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Lucy-Rose/150865674950117?sk=wall"><b>Facebook</b></a> / <a href="http://twitter.com/lucyrosemusic"><b>Twitter</b></a></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">We picked up on her '<a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/11/ep-review-lucy-rose-middle-of-bed.html"><b>Middle Of The Bed</b></a>' EP at the tail end of last year, and with new single '<b>Red Face</b>' carrying on where she left off, <b>Lucy Rose</b> is certainly attracting our attention. Recording has begun on her debut album which we can't wait to hear when its drops later this year.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="http://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F32571193&amp;show_artwork=true" width="100%"></iframe></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><u><b><span style="font-size: x-large;">Pale Seas</span></b></u> <span style="font-size: x-small;">//</span> <span style="font-size: x-small;"><a href="http://www.facebook.com/paleseas"><b>Facebook</b></a></span> </div><div style="text-align: justify;">Last year a band called <b>Netherlands</b> put out a low key release of their track '<b>Sooner Or Later</b>', which made <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/12/music-liberations-top-5-tracks-of-2011.html"><b>Music Liberation's Top 5 Singles of 2011</b></a>. Well that band are now called <b>Pale Seas</b>, and that track is set to receive alot more attention. We are hungry for more, much more!</div>||
Music Liberation's Writers takeover week : Moker|<div style="text-align: justify;">To round off the Music Liberation's Writers takeover week we have <a href="https://twitter.com/#%21/musicgob"><b>Moker</b></a>... </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-cNKuCSF5ehI/Twc6dP4Lf-I/AAAAAAAADXk/9u_4neQb5eI/s1600/jm_twathat.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-cNKuCSF5ehI/Twc6dP4Lf-I/AAAAAAAADXk/9u_4neQb5eI/s1600/jm_twathat.jpg"/></a>"Well this is a little surprising. Looking back at the artists I’ve managed to review in 2011, the one thing that’s abundantly clear is that I’ve heavily favoured music with female vocals and shoegaze, layered guitars. This must be some kind of subconscious shift in my tastes as I’d never have normally ticked such boxes if I had to describe my favourite music. I’m pleasantly surprised. It’s a bit the reverse of when you go through your record collection and wonder why there’s so much awful metal in there. Or is that just me? (<i>ED: Nope!</i>)</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Anyway, out of the all the reviews this year, my three favourite would have to be <b>Sea Oleena’s</b> beautiful new EP, the New York duo <b>Acrylics</b> single ‘<i>Molly’s Vertigo</i>’ and <b>EMA’s</b> fantastic debut album ‘<i>Past Life and Martyred Saints</i>’.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">If I had to rank these three in order (and I do) it would go as such:</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Rr5m1Yx3wGM/Twc-rQibMYI/AAAAAAAADX0/ln_byv7ouVQ/s1600/acrylics.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Rr5m1Yx3wGM/Twc-rQibMYI/AAAAAAAADX0/ln_byv7ouVQ/s1600/acrylics.jpg"/></a>3) <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/08/single-review-acrylics-mollys-vertigo.html"><b>Acrylics - Molly's Vertigo</b></a> : If only because it was a single review rather than a whole body of work. This dreamy 80s tinged pop song was truly fantastic.  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/#%21/pages/Acrylics/162211760462307"><b>Acrylics</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4DOjLls4dgA/Twc-UjdxPFI/AAAAAAAADXs/iO0exAMXghQ/s1600/ema.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4DOjLls4dgA/Twc-UjdxPFI/AAAAAAAADXs/iO0exAMXghQ/s1600/ema.jpg"/></a> </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">2) <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/07/album-review-ema-past-life-martyred.html"><b>EMA - Past Life Martyred Saints</b></a> : Already in many critics’ top ten lists, this wide-ranging and off-kilter debut is a true masterpiece. I wrote that it sounds as if she was on the verge of a breakdown and letting every emotion flow out into the music and I stand by that verbose description; perhaps because it’s a gloriously verbose record in all the right ways. Every listen will bring something new. Also album opener ‘<b>The Grey Ship</b>’ is a worthy contender for Single of 2011.  <a href="http://cameouttanowhere.com/"><b>EMA</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-WrIQHw_U_b4/Twc_KptUSoI/AAAAAAAADYE/qElLmZkdFig/s1600/sea+oleena.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-WrIQHw_U_b4/Twc_KptUSoI/AAAAAAAADYE/qElLmZkdFig/s1600/sea+oleena.jpg"/></a>1) <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/12/ep-review-sea-oleena-sleeplessness.html"><b>Sea Oleena - Sleeplessness</b></a> : There’s no escaping the beauty of <b>Sea Oleena’s</b> music. Both her most recent EP and her self-titled debut are an intoxicating mix of ghostly vocals and layered ambient noise. Intimate, emotive and leftfield, she’s been my favourite find of this year.  <a href="http://seaoleena.bandcamp.com/"><b>Sea Oleena</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="http://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F14693031&amp;show_artwork=true" width="100%"></iframe><br/><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-kjcDICle4u8/Twc_u2aV7FI/AAAAAAAADYM/lDOkvG7H9Og/s1600/372953_7722198515_977887147_q.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-kjcDICle4u8/Twc_u2aV7FI/AAAAAAAADYM/lDOkvG7H9Og/s1600/372953_7722198515_977887147_q.jpg"/></a>With regards to next year, there are a few artists on my radar who are worth keeping an eye out for. The first is angular metal band <a href="http://alrightthecaptain.bandcamp.com/"><b>Alright the Captain</b></a>. Their album was released all the way back in January and despite being a perfect slab of relentless jagged noise, it didn’t get the coverage it deserved.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-QP41mlCFZYE/TwdBoGa40jI/AAAAAAAADYU/SWALWncyqr4/s1600/pengillys.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-QP41mlCFZYE/TwdBoGa40jI/AAAAAAAADYU/SWALWncyqr4/s1600/pengillys.jpg"/></a>The second recommendation would be a band from the North of England called <a href="http://pengillys.bandcamp.com/"><b>Pengilly’s</b></a>. An unusual name for an unusual band. Their honest, heartfelt and spacious approach to music is a little like a folk band remixed by <i>James Blake</i>. The future can only be bright for these trendsetters. (<i>ED: The keen eyed amongst you will remember we featured Pengilly's on <b>Music Liberation</b> back in September with the video for '<a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/09/new-video-pengillys-tobys-hill.html"><b>Toby's Hill</b></a>'.</i>)</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-PNaYaGrfL_U/TwdCGDYdt-I/AAAAAAAADYc/_5EgDkyVH88/s1600/276956_8298733825_1605778136_q.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-PNaYaGrfL_U/TwdCGDYdt-I/AAAAAAAADYc/_5EgDkyVH88/s1600/276956_8298733825_1605778136_q.jpg"/></a>The final recommendation would be the well established and long running Belgium electro band <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/GOOSE/8298733825"><b>Goose</b></a>. Some might know of them but I’ve listed them here as they’ve always been at the peripheries of the funky house scene, dominated by French acts such as <i>Daft Punk</i> and <i>Justice</i>. They most recent album, released last year was superb and surely the high profile coverage they deserve should come to them off the back of their fantastic efforts.</div>||
Music Liberation's Writers takeover week : Clive Rozario|<div style="text-align: justify;"> Here's <a href="http://twitter.com/#%21/cliverozario"><b>Clive Rozario</b></a> with his thoughts on 2011 and his tips for the forthcoming year.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-1Rtxxx0UmsQ/TwXGhvFxV7I/AAAAAAAADV0/jufsH_Y-duQ/s1600/n60506349_33038997_9283_bigger.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-1Rtxxx0UmsQ/TwXGhvFxV7I/AAAAAAAADV0/jufsH_Y-duQ/s1600/n60506349_33038997_9283_bigger.jpg"/></a>"Do you know what I told myself on New Year's Day, 2011? I promised that after burning myself out in 2010 attending endless gigs, squandering (the majority of my) funds on an unnecessary eight festivals, clogging up my accommodation with Cd's that were only used once (to upload to my iPod), and destroying my Mac with an addiction to downloading new music, that I would take it a little easier - music-wise - in 2011. Do you know what I told myself on New Year's Day, 2012? I promised myself that since 2011's equally relentless musical year not only burnt me out, but actually gave me tinnitus, I <b>WILL</b> take it a little easier in 2012…</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">We had some huge records last year: <i>Metronomy</i>, <i>Machine Head</i>, <i>SBTRKT</i>, <i>James Blake</i>, <i>Bon Iver</i>, letlive., <i>Jamie Woon</i>, <i>Radiohead</i>, <i>Mazes</i>, <i>Gil Scott Heron &amp; Jamie XX</i>, <i>City and Colour</i>, <i>Mastodon</i>, etc. However, some of the most enjoyable music I have encountered this year has been from the underground, in the form of independent albums or debut EPs and whatnot.<br/><br/>Here is my TOP 3 from the releases I've covered for <b>Music Liberation</b> in 2011:</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-UnR040isJrg/TwXHJP8g_-I/AAAAAAAADWA/tzgrmtcFSaE/s1600/qd.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-UnR040isJrg/TwXHJP8g_-I/AAAAAAAADWA/tzgrmtcFSaE/s1600/qd.jpg"/></a> 1. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/06/ep-review-quick-and-dead-for-rhythm.html"><b>Quick and The Dead - 'For The Rhythm'</b></a> - This little, pop punk-tinged emo EP came armed with a surprisingly full production, and some massive, massive vocal hooks. The epic title track rivals anything <i>Taking Back Sunday</i>, <i>Funeral For A Friend</i>, <i>Kids In Glass Houses</i> etc. have done. (<i>ED: Unfortunately QATD decided at the back end of last year to split up</i>)  <a href="http://www.quickandthedead.co.uk/"><b>Quick And The Dead</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/>2. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/05/ep-review-vetoes-ritalinritalout.html"><b>Vetoes - 'Ritalin/Ritalout'</b></a> - I'm still none-the-wiser about whether the term 'post-prog' has actually become a fully fledged genre, but the urgency of this progressive mash-up of math-rock and alternative indie has stayed with me all year. '<b>Sonic Turge</b>' is a tune!  <a href="http://www.myspace.com/vetoes"><b>Vetoes</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="http://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F10693152&amp;show_artwork=true" width="100%"></iframe><br/><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/>3. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/07/album-review-shapes-monotony-chic.html"><b>Shapes - 'Monotony Chic'</b></a> - The debut album from this noisy post-hardcore mob may lacked real originality (sounding a fair bit like <i>letlive.</i>, who sound more than a fait bit like <i>Glassjaw</i>), but they made up for it with punishing technicality and an impassioned vocal performance. Check out '<b>Vacancy Ape</b>' - the album highlight.  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/#%21/weareshapes"><b>Shapes</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/><iframe frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="http://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F19888411&amp;show_artwork=true" width="100%"></iframe><br/><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">*A special mention must be made for We'll Go Machete's album '<a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/09/album-review-well-go-machete-strong.html"><b>Strong Drunk Hands</b></a>', which only just missed out on the TOP 3.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Now for the Tips for 2012: new artists I think are going to have a great year.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-bv0WtKwAF2s/TwXNG1-pcwI/AAAAAAAADXU/8Im3DFoTkyM/s1600/276503_172295042826449_299821178_q.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-bv0WtKwAF2s/TwXNG1-pcwI/AAAAAAAADXU/8Im3DFoTkyM/s1600/276503_172295042826449_299821178_q.jpg"/></a>1. <u><b>Drive</b></u> - This Hertfordshire quartet are shrouded in mystery. Having only formed last year, they released a dreamy little demo called '<b>No Feel</b>' (after only having been together a month!), which was picked up by the blogosphere with all it's heart. I mean, this replication of shoegazing-tinted, noise-rock, alternative bands like <i>My Bloody Valentine</i> and <i>Sonic Youth</i> was addictive in its authenticity - the word 'nostalgic' didn't even come to mind. Little is known about the band (as they have pretty much no online presence), but i'm sure we'll be hearing more from them in 2012.  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/drivetheband"><b>Drive</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-NJiTOCpEIVs/TwXKfD_EmjI/AAAAAAAADWw/oIwtCuE42FQ/s1600/373102_95107627835_494219528_q.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-NJiTOCpEIVs/TwXKfD_EmjI/AAAAAAAADWw/oIwtCuE42FQ/s1600/373102_95107627835_494219528_q.jpg"/></a>2. <u><b>Blue Daisy</b></u> - The London producer's recently released, debut album '<b>The Sunday Gift</b>' has received critical acclaim, but it's one of those slow-burners - electronica fans are only just starting to really pick up on the moody dubstep-laced triphop, and it's 2012 that is going to see his name truly made.  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/Bluedaisyofficial"><b>Blue Daisy</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-bGwMYJX5sqc/TwXM03wdwJI/AAAAAAAADXI/I62pn3tW7_w/s1600/373125_24200315632_1784123955_q.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-bGwMYJX5sqc/TwXM03wdwJI/AAAAAAAADXI/I62pn3tW7_w/s1600/373125_24200315632_1784123955_q.jpg"/></a>3. <u><b>Casitas</b></u> - The quirky indie-party-pop band from Devon have been quiet since releasing their independent, self-titled debut, and winning a plethora of 'battle of the bands' comps. They are apparently in the process of (slowly) making their follow-up, and are dedicating 2012 to radically expanding their fanbase. Check out their track '<b>Lykke Lii</b>'.  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/The-Casitas/24200315632"><b>Casitas</b></a></div>||
Music Liberation's Writers takeover week : Chris Meredith|<div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-IYRtgXxlA0w/TwRAxTq8hCI/AAAAAAAADUU/pklnQ24QQIk/s1600/Hotchkiss_reasonably_small.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-IYRtgXxlA0w/TwRAxTq8hCI/AAAAAAAADUU/pklnQ24QQIk/s1600/Hotchkiss_reasonably_small.jpg"/></a>Day 2 of the Music Liberation Writers takeover week. <a href="http://twitter.com/#%21/cfmeredith"><b>Chris Meredith</b></a> picks his favourite reviews of 2011 and gives us his tips for the year ahead. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"My top 3 reviews are:</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">1) <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/08/single-review-bullitts-jay-electronica.html"><b>     The Bullitts &amp; Jay Electronica – Run and Hide</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;">2)      <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/07/ep-review-modual-in-all-kinds.html"><b>Modual- In all Kinds</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;">3)      <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/02/new-music-seri-doja.html"><b>Seri Doja</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-lZgtPhMRuLA/TwRBkBv6IEI/AAAAAAAADUs/K2yNsYAn5gc/s1600/bullitts.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-lZgtPhMRuLA/TwRBkBv6IEI/AAAAAAAADUs/K2yNsYAn5gc/s1600/bullitts.jpg"/></a>The reason I selected The Bullitts and Jay Elec as number 1 was due to how I felt the track was taking hip-hop into a new era that we are still yet to see the fruits of. <b> Jay Electronica</b> is one of the most exciting talents in Hip Hop who has still to drop an album and one definitely to look out for in 2012.  <b>The Bullitts</b> creativity and eye for an excellent piece of cinematography to compliment their music is something quite extraordinary.  <b>James Samuel</b>, who is the creative force behind The Bullitts is another artist who will be pushing the limits of where music can take you in 2012."  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/thebullitts"><b>The Bullitts</b></a> // <a href="http://www.jay-electronica.com/"><b>Jay Electronica</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/><iframe class="html5player" frameborder="no" height="166" scrolling="no" src="http://w.soundcloud.com/player/?url=http%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F19982131&amp;show_artwork=true" width="100%"></iframe><br/><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">These are the artists I'm looking forward to hearing more from in 2012:</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"></div><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ZWpaSOEvObk/TwRGqc3WApI/AAAAAAAADVE/8RhDLFDXhWY/s1600/261157_199783721267_1789525_q.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ZWpaSOEvObk/TwRGqc3WApI/AAAAAAAADVE/8RhDLFDXhWY/s1600/261157_199783721267_1789525_q.jpg"/></a><u><b>Keaton Henson</b></u> – Keaton is an extremely fragile and talented individual whose music and art complement each other in such a way it just makes you stop and think (check the video for <a href="http://vimeo.com/20332336"><b>Charad</b></a> to confirm this).  His voice is as fragile and raw as his appearance and will leave you asking yourself why you ever listened to <i>Ed Sheeran</i>!  <a href="http://www.keatonhenson.com/"><b>Keaton Henson</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-FF9zTRqQAec/TwRHZqytDDI/AAAAAAAADVQ/FV-JN36ykLM/s1600/372976_178491792181607_1191405112_q.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-FF9zTRqQAec/TwRHZqytDDI/AAAAAAAADVQ/FV-JN36ykLM/s1600/372976_178491792181607_1191405112_q.jpg"/></a><u><b>Cloud Boat</b></u> – Cload Boat are an electronic duo from <a href="http://rsrecords.com/"><b>R&amp;S Records</b></a> and ever since I saw them support <i>James Blake</i> in Cardiff early last year a week doesn’t go by where I’m not looking for new material.  '<i>Lions on the Beach</i>' would be their break through single for last year, but I am eagerly anticipating their EP which drops in 2012.  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/cloudboat"><b>Cloud Boat</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-cziWZGBmYKY/TwRJ3LaiwpI/AAAAAAAADVo/_mVMHaUoFh0/s1600/372867_19065274432_1509580186_q.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-cziWZGBmYKY/TwRJ3LaiwpI/AAAAAAAADVo/_mVMHaUoFh0/s1600/372867_19065274432_1509580186_q.jpg"/></a><u><b>Architects</b></u> – A band that has been tearing the roof off of venues for a long time now, but they seem to have made a way into the ears of the mainstream through gigs and festivals throughout 2011.  Whatever genre you want to classify this band under (deathcore/hardcore would be most appropriate), this is a group who I just can’t take my eye off.  The band has recently released the single '<b>Devil’s Island</b>' whilst on tour in the UK, which shows signs of new music for 2012.  This band is heart thumping rage at its best and something that they exuberate when performing live.  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/architectsuk"><b>Architects</b></a></div>||
Music Liberation's Writers takeover week : Tom Nash|<div style="text-align: justify;">This week <b>Music Liberation</b> is being taken over exclusively by its' fine collection of <a href="http://www.musicliberation.blogspot.com/p/writers.html"><b>Writers</b></a>, as I, Mr 'Editor', hang up my boots and have a week off before we get back into the usual new music loving swing of things next week.<br/><br/><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-lUcWhxAhPvc/TwM4KvU8Z9I/AAAAAAAADTA/jtph5CKL2SE/s1600/Photo_on_2010-10-19_at_17.01_reasonably_small.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-lUcWhxAhPvc/TwM4KvU8Z9I/AAAAAAAADTA/jtph5CKL2SE/s1600/Photo_on_2010-10-19_at_17.01_reasonably_small.jpg"/></a>First up, our newest writer, <a href="https://twitter.com/#%21/thewritetomnash"><b>Tom Nash</b></a>, kicks things off by choosing his favourite review of 2011.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Coming to the ML team late in the year, I only covered two releases; <i>Dilated Peoples</i> emcee <b>Evidence’s</b> second solo album <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/11/album-review-evidence-cats-dogs.html"><b>Cats &amp; Dogs</b></a> and <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/11/album-review-hectic-zeniths-hectic.html"><b>Hectic Zeniths’</b></a> self-titled debut.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-wF49cSvSXyU/TwM6hr5B5BI/AAAAAAAADTw/9RHJLulIwys/s1600/Evidence-Cats-Dogs-Artwork.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="200" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-wF49cSvSXyU/TwM6hr5B5BI/AAAAAAAADTw/9RHJLulIwys/s200/Evidence-Cats-Dogs-Artwork.jpg" width="200"/></a><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Zo88vUSiOAo/TwM6YGqY5yI/AAAAAAAADTk/xlwfDxaJGtc/s1600/2243870907-1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="200" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Zo88vUSiOAo/TwM6YGqY5yI/AAAAAAAADTk/xlwfDxaJGtc/s200/2243870907-1.jpg" width="200"/></a><br/>With just two albums to choose from, you’d think it would be simple picking a favourite. It wasn’t. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The thumping boom-bap and laidback West Coast vibes of <b>Cats &amp; Dogs</b> was refreshing in a year when mainstream Hip Hop was dominated by heavy synths and House-inspired floor fillers, whereas <b>Hectic Zeniths</b> provided an LP packed full of dramatic keys and strings that was perfect for shoe-gazing on a cold morning or as the soundtrack to a chill evening.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">So which to choose?</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">While <b>Evidence</b> has turned out a strong album in a year of great releases, my vote goes to the newcomer: <b>Hectic Zeniths</b>. Each track is a beautifully crafted, multi-layered soundscape, which makes the album a wonderfully evocative experience that is just crying out for repeat listens.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">With such a strong debut, Hectic Zeniths has set the bar high for future releases, but I for one, will be eagerly anticipating any new music from this exciting new artist.<br/><br/><a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/11/album-review-evidence-cats-dogs.html"><b>Evidence - Cats And Dogs</b></a> (Album Review - 21st November)  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/misterevidence"><b>Evidence</b></a><br/><br/><a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/11/album-review-hectic-zeniths-hectic.html"><b>Hectic Zeniths - Hectic Zeniths</b></a> (Album Review - 29th November)  <a href="http://hecticzeniths.bandcamp.com/"><b>Hectic Zeniths</b></a></div>||
The Blog Sound of 2012 : The Top 5|||
Music Liberation's Top 10 Albums of 2011|<div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-vOhFOhJ6euA/Tv8T3dCt4dI/AAAAAAAADQY/rZRUvwMoeW4/s1600/mazes.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-vOhFOhJ6euA/Tv8T3dCt4dI/AAAAAAAADQY/rZRUvwMoeW4/s1600/mazes.jpg"/></a>3. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/04/album-review-mazes-thousand-heys.html"><b>Mazes - A Thousand Heys</b></a> <span style="font-size: x-small;">// Reviewed 18th April by <a href="http://www.twitter.com/jonsidwell">Jon Sidwell</a></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Album opener '<b>Go Betweens</b>' sets  the tone of the record, with simple, pacey drums interspersed with  scuzzy energetic guitars and playful yet punchy vocals from frontman <b>Jack Cooper</b>. '<b>Surf &amp; Turf / Maths Tag</b>' demonstrates the bands ear for tempo changes, where as '<b>Most Days</b>' is them at their most ferocious. <b>A Thousand Heys</b> is a  fun, chaotic, frenzied, emotional roller coaster of a debut record that  will have you hitting the repeat button throughout the forthcoming  Summer."  <a href="http://www.myspace.com/mazesmazesmazes"><b>Mazes</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-qPGIKpNoxhU/Tv8UtQUzecI/AAAAAAAADQk/vcczX4vot3g/s1600/shapes.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-qPGIKpNoxhU/Tv8UtQUzecI/AAAAAAAADQk/vcczX4vot3g/s1600/shapes.jpg"/></a>4. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/07/album-review-shapes-monotony-chic.html"><b>Shapes - Monotony Chic</b></a> <span style="font-size: x-small;">// Reviewed 27th July by <a href="http://twitter.com/#%21/cliverozario">Clive Rozario</a></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"This is an urgent and intense collection of songs worthy of your time. And time is something it may need, as ‘<b>Monotony Chic</b>’  does take a couple listens for the tunes to sink in. It may sound a  little erratic and messy at first, but there is real precision here, and  it may only be on the third listen that you begin to distinguish  between riffs (and man are some of the riffs nice!), screams, and time  signatures."  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/#%21/weareshapes"><b>Shapes</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-834PSBmgSmQ/Tv8VubTYaKI/AAAAAAAADQw/50ejsTQOA_8/s1600/evidence.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-834PSBmgSmQ/Tv8VubTYaKI/AAAAAAAADQw/50ejsTQOA_8/s1600/evidence.jpg"/></a>5. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/11/album-review-evidence-cats-dogs.html"><b>Evidence - Cats and Dogs</b></a> <span style="font-size: x-small;">// Reviewed 21st November by <a href="http://twitter.com/thewritetomnash">Tom Nash</a></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"With no trace of a radio-friendly single or a floor-filling club banger, <b>Cats &amp; Dogs</b> may not win <b>Evidence</b>  new fans, but after two decades in the business, it is clear that isn’t  important to him. He knows his strengths and he plays to them. If you like whiplash-inducing beats and solid rhymes, you won’t go wrong with this LP."  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/misterevidence"><b>Evidence</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-v5Le2WdNOjY/Tv8XBNKWYHI/AAAAAAAADQ8/j3s8Fj2XNvk/s1600/nz.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-v5Le2WdNOjY/Tv8XBNKWYHI/AAAAAAAADQ8/j3s8Fj2XNvk/s1600/nz.jpg"/></a>6. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/11/album-review-hectic-zeniths-hectic.html"><b>Hectic Zeniths - Hectic Zeniths</b></a><span style="font-size: x-small;"> // Reviewed 29th November by <a href="http://twitter.com/thewritetomnash">Tom Nash</a></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"While never reaching their cinematic heights, <b>Hectic Zeniths</b> draws comparisons with <i>Blue Sky Black Death</i> or <i>Emancipator</i>,  each known for creating rich and densely layered music. At eleven  tracks long and clocking in at half an hour from beginning to end, some  may feel it may be on the short side, but with each song containing so  many elements, replay value will undoubtedly be high."  <a href="http://hecticzeniths.bandcamp.com/"><b>Hectic Zeniths</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-BPG-m7jdyVc/Tv8X0ZBQEuI/AAAAAAAADRI/-yxVsp1u8pw/s1600/me.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-BPG-m7jdyVc/Tv8X0ZBQEuI/AAAAAAAADRI/-yxVsp1u8pw/s1600/me.jpg"/></a>7. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/05/album-review-munroe-effect.html"><b>Munroe Effect - Ultraviolenceland</b></a> // <span style="font-size: x-small;">Reviewed 30th May by <a href="http://www.twitter.com/jonsidwell">Jon Sidwell</a></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Delivering a much needed and long overdue shot in the arm of a stagnant post-hardcore scene, Portsmouth’s <b>Munroe Effect</b> this week finally unveil their debut album ‘<b>Ultraviolenceland</b>’. Released through <b>Dead Plant Records</b>, and mastered by <b>Alan Douche</b> (<i>Dillinger Escape Plan</i>, <i>Brand New</i>)  this record reveals a band who sound equally at home flailing chaotic  guitars around, as they are laying down soaring melodies."  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/munroeeffect"><b>Munroe Effect</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-6W6k4RimpgY/Tv8Yilq3bcI/AAAAAAAADRU/7TZp5VJgGgk/s1600/cm.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-6W6k4RimpgY/Tv8Yilq3bcI/AAAAAAAADRU/7TZp5VJgGgk/s1600/cm.jpg"/></a>8. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/05/album-review-crooked-mountain-crooked.html"><b>Crooked Mountain, Crooked Sea - Whats There To Write About</b></a> <span style="font-size: x-small;">// Reviewed 4th May by <a href="http://www.twitter.com/jonsidwell">Jon Sidwell</a></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Clocking in at a mere 27 minutes there  no hanging around with this record, but then there’s enough diversity  on offer to make it somehow seem longer than that. Having been recorded  predominantly live in a converted stable there is a tendency for some  sounds to get drowned out by others, however I feel this adds great  texture and a sense of urgency. This debut record is raw and totally uncompromising, certainly not for the faint of heart, but well worth checking out."  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/crookedmountaincrookedsea"><b>Crooked Mountain, Crooked Sea</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-5BsMskwPT4Q/Tv8ZvQTSoKI/AAAAAAAADRg/Swtc280EUDg/s1600/ea.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-5BsMskwPT4Q/Tv8ZvQTSoKI/AAAAAAAADRg/Swtc280EUDg/s1600/ea.jpg"/></a>9. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/06/album-review-everyone-to-anderson-man.html"><b>Everyone To The Anderson - The Man Born From Inside Of A Horse</b></a> <span style="font-size: x-small;">// Reviewed 17th June by <a href="http://www.twitter.com/jonsidwell">Jon Sidwell</a></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Kicking off with '<b>High Brow, Low Brow, No Eye Brow</b>' (possible reference to '<i>High Five, Swan Dive, Nose Dive</i>' by <i>Pulled Apart By Horses</i>?  meh...) the band launch into their mathy guitar driven noise, with  yelpy stop start vocals from Ben Gregory, supported by driven yet  understated drums. Instant comparisons can be drawn with <i>Foals</i> ('Antidotes' era), and contemporaries such as <i>Future Of The Left</i> and <i>Les Savy Fav</i>."  <b><a href="https://www.facebook.com/#%21/everyonetotheanderson">Everyone To The Anderson</a></b></div>||
Music Liberation's Top 5 EPs of 2011|<div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-GGZa2n6gPlo/TvxzS8ZCV3I/AAAAAAAADPE/eDbE-mS9-b0/s1600/daughter.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-GGZa2n6gPlo/TvxzS8ZCV3I/AAAAAAAADPE/eDbE-mS9-b0/s1600/daughter.jpg"/></a>1. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/12/ep-review-daughter-wild-youth.html"><b>Daughter - The Wild Youth</b></a> <span style="font-size: x-small;"><i>// Reviewed 9th December by <a href="http://www.twitter.com/jonsidwell">Jon Sidwell</a></i></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Elena and Igor have an ear to create space within their music, moments  where their instruments can breath and the listener can fully appreciate  the beauty that is being played out before them. The poignant  combination of Elena's lingering vocals and the delicate  acoustic/electric guitars demonstrate how simplicity in music is  something to be applauded."  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/ohdaughter"><b>Daughter</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-BWWmVJ9B-Ak/Tvx0J7pQtEI/AAAAAAAADPQ/tOwa0b4is0Q/s1600/kids.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-BWWmVJ9B-Ak/Tvx0J7pQtEI/AAAAAAAADPQ/tOwa0b4is0Q/s1600/kids.jpg"/></a>2. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/08/ep-review-girls-summer-frights.html"><b>Kids  - Summer Frights</b></a> <span style="font-size: x-small;"><i>// Reviewed 3rd August by <a href="http://www.twitter.com/jonsidwell">Jon Sidwell</a></i></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: x-small;"><i> </i></span>"San Diego's <b>Kids</b> have delivered one of the most refreshing records I have come across so far this year in the shape of their debut EP '<b>Summer Frights</b>'. What makes this even more delightful and impressive is that the 5-piece (<i>Nature</i>, <i>Cory</i>, <i>Blake</i>, <i>Ben</i>, and <i>Matt</i>) all between the ages of just 17 and 19. <b>Kids</b>, appropriately titled then."  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/#%21/kidskidskids"><b>Kids</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-pdg7AO1notA/Tvx1NjaXJ0I/AAAAAAAADPc/lb-3fBPga_Y/s1600/sea+oleena.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-pdg7AO1notA/Tvx1NjaXJ0I/AAAAAAAADPc/lb-3fBPga_Y/s1600/sea+oleena.jpg"/></a> 3. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/12/ep-review-sea-oleena-sleeplessness.html"><b>Sea Oleena - Sleeplessness</b></a> <span style="font-size: x-small;"><i>// Reviewed 15th December by <a href="https://twitter.com/#%21/musicgob">Moker</a></i></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Standing at seven tracks in length, <b>Sea Oleena’s</b> new release '<b>Sleeplessness</b>'  could be considered more mini-album than EP, but that still wouldn’t  justify the enormity of the music recorded by Montréal  multi-instrumentalist<b> Charlotte Loseth</b>. The record is a beautiful  warm blanket of songs, each one an epic cacophony of layered sounds,  reverb and haunting female vocals delivered with the unassuming charm of  a girl humming a song in her bedroom."  <a href="http://seaoleena.bandcamp.com/"><b>Sea Oleena</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-UR2Esnku6L4/Tvx2J0kC9rI/AAAAAAAADPo/eXcsfUt7mYU/s1600/lightguides.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-UR2Esnku6L4/Tvx2J0kC9rI/AAAAAAAADPo/eXcsfUt7mYU/s1600/lightguides.jpg"/></a>4. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/10/ep-review-lightguides-samba-samba-samba.html"><b>Lightguides - Samba Samba Samba</b></a> <span style="font-size: x-small;"><i>// Reviewed 4th October by <a href="http://www.twitter.com/jonsidwell">Jon Sidwell</a></i></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: x-small;"><i>"</i></span><b>Samba Samba Samba</b> is a record that will put a smile on your  face when you're feeling down, get you in the mood to go out and party,  or even for those times when you need to reflect. It's an all  encompassing album from a band who clearly have the talents and the  mindset to reach as many heads and hearts as they please."  <a href="http://lightguidesmusic.co.uk/"><b>Lightguides</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-0mqGYlw9G84/Tvx3Cg0YfBI/AAAAAAAADP0/kUbLIf8peT4/s1600/gunning+for+tamar.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-0mqGYlw9G84/Tvx3Cg0YfBI/AAAAAAAADP0/kUbLIf8peT4/s1600/gunning+for+tamar.jpg"/></a>5.<b> <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/04/ep-review-gunning-for-tamar-deaf-cow.html">Gunning For Tamar - Deaf Cow Motel</a> </b><span style="font-size: x-small;"><i>// Reviewed 21st April by <a href="http://twitter.com/#%21/cliverozario">Clive Rozario</a></i></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: x-small;"><i> </i></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"A big feature of <b>Gunning For Tamar’s</b> post-hardcore that sets them apart  from the competition is the epic and emotive vocals – containing both  gentle vulnerability and commanding strength. These (scream-free)  vocals, together with the general intricate nature of the layered  guitars, recall the intelligent emo of <i>Funeral For A Friend’s</i> ‘<i>Memory And Humanity</i>.’ And just like FFAF, Gunning For Tamar are able to sound both progressive and accessible through their soaring melodies."  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Gunning-For-Tamar/204699357276?sk=wall"><b>Gunning For Tamar</b></a></div>||
Music Liberation's Top 5 Tracks of 2011|<div style="text-align: justify;">We begin our round up of this year with our top 5 tracks that we reviewed in 2011. This will be followed later this week by our top 5 EPs, Music Liberation writers picks of the year, and finally our top 10 albums of the year...</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-thfSHbg5DxA/TvmyQQPj9wI/AAAAAAAADN8/rbksnxb6KVM/s1600/safe_image.php.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-thfSHbg5DxA/TvmyQQPj9wI/AAAAAAAADN8/rbksnxb6KVM/s1600/safe_image.php.jpg"/></a>1. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/11/single-review-cloud-nothings-no-future.html"><b>Cloud Nothings - No Future / No Past</b></a> <i>// <span style="font-size: x-small;">Reviewed November 18th by <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/search/label/Jon%20Sidwell">Jon Sidwell</a></span></i></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Beginning in a haunting fashion with distant piano and slow methodical bass and drums, front man <b>Dylan Baldi</b>  croaks in an ever demanding voice as the music slowly builds and  builds. And keep it keeps building until the wheels start to fall off,  but the band keep going, with Baldi’s call to arm shouts of “<i>No future, no past</i>” surrounded by crashing drums and flailing guitars."  <b><a href="http://www.facebook.com/cloudnothings">Cloud Nothings</a></b></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-H809QENn4mA/Tvm1YEnKmwI/AAAAAAAADOI/Urunzin-BTY/s1600/dead+red+sun.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-H809QENn4mA/Tvm1YEnKmwI/AAAAAAAADOI/Urunzin-BTY/s1600/dead+red+sun.jpg"/></a>2. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/02/single-review-dead-red-sun-facility.html"><b>Dead Red Sun - Facility</b></a> <span style="font-size: x-small;"><i>//</i></span> <i><span style="font-size: x-small;">Reviewed 1st February by <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/search/label/Jon%20Sidwell">Jon Sidwell</a></span></i></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Opening with a recorded voice sample, things quickly move  into instrumental territory as <b>Mike Guppy's</b> guitar, <b>Ollie Bremner's</b> bass, and <b>Tom Murphy's</b> drums all collide with pin point precision. The pace is fast and  unnerving, making the listener acutely aware that a full on crescendo is  about to occur, and it dutifully does just over halfway through the  track."  <a href="http://deadredsun.bandcamp.com/"><b>Dead Red Sun</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-bQuGCQ1JDK0/Tvm3Cj3JyKI/AAAAAAAADOU/cWYsMjEIVoQ/s1600/the+bullitts.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-bQuGCQ1JDK0/Tvm3Cj3JyKI/AAAAAAAADOU/cWYsMjEIVoQ/s1600/the+bullitts.jpg"/></a>3. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/08/single-review-bullitts-jay-electronica.html"><b>The Bullitts - Run And Hide (Feat. Jay Electronica)</b></a> <span style="font-size: x-small;"><i>// Reviewed 17th August by <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/search/label/Chris%20Meredith">Chris Meredith</a></i></span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"The Bullitts are making musical masterpieces and Jaymes isn’t just  satisfied with the soundtrack, he wants you to picture the inspiration  behind the production. With '<b>Run</b> <b>and</b> <b>Hide</b>' he has  combined French cinema production, with a soulful and simple backing  vocal, to which Jay Elec’ adds the finishing touch to what makes this  track an absolute smash." <a href="http://thebullitts.com/enter.html"><b>The Bullitts</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-BkDV_jRsHHY/Tvm4nwG-6HI/AAAAAAAADOg/hjhSjAIANao/s1600/netherlands.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-BkDV_jRsHHY/Tvm4nwG-6HI/AAAAAAAADOg/hjhSjAIANao/s1600/netherlands.jpg"/></a>4. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/09/single-review-netherlands-something-or.html"><b>Netherlands - Something Or Nothing</b></a> <i><span style="font-size: x-small;">// Reviewed 5th September by <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/search/label/Jon%20Sidwell">Jon Sidwell</a></span></i> <span style="font-size: x-small;">(NB: Netherlands now renamed <a href="http://www.facebook.com/paleseas">Pale Seas</a>)</span></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"Starting with some fluttering wind chimes &amp; muted guitars, the track gently floats into pop/folk motion with the vocals of <b>Jacob Scotts</b>.  His voice is delicate &amp; vulnerable and fits the tender music perfectly. If you don't end up swaying along to this one then you've got  serious balance issues. The harmonies are infectious, &amp; repeated  listens only further the addiction to this band and  their sound."</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-t-2gGCYJF3s/Tvm7if9SDsI/AAAAAAAADO4/oCKUaN2XzXM/s1600/acrylics.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-t-2gGCYJF3s/Tvm7if9SDsI/AAAAAAAADO4/oCKUaN2XzXM/s1600/acrylics.jpg"/></a>5. <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/08/single-review-acrylics-mollys-vertigo.html"><b>Acrylics - Molly's Vertigo</b></a> <span style="font-size: x-small;"><i>// Reviewed 15th August by <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/search/label/Moker">Moker</a></i></span><br/>"Take it with a pinch of British salt when I say the new single from Brooklyn based <b>Acrylics</b>  is so good, I knew it had to originate from across the water. Whether  or not I might be culturally bias towards the Americans doesn’t stop ‘<b>Molly’s Vertigo</b>’ from being an atmospheric, 80s tinged pop ballad of perfection." <a href="http://www.facebook.com/#%21/pages/Acrylics/162211760462307"><b>Acrylics</b></a> </div>||
Merry Christmas 2011|||
EP Review : Likes Lions - Future Colour|<div style="text-align: justify;"><b>Likes Lions</b> are an alternative rock quintet from Sheffield, UK. They are not the indie band <i>In Like Lions</i>, nor are they the electro-pop band <i>Live Like Lions</i>. And they are certainly not the hardcore punk band <i>Like Lions</i> from New York. Ever heard of SEO boys?</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">This <b>Likes Lions</b> formed in 2009, and '<b>Future Colour</b>' - released in October 2011 - is their debut EP. They take the more accessible aspects of math-rock and post-rock, and fuse them together to produce a heavier, Foals-esque, indie sound. For some reason (perhaps due to the massive success of the aforementioned <i>Foals</i>), I have ended up reviewing a few too many math-indie-rock EPs this year. However, Likes Lions melody-conscious take on the genre made this a somewhat enjoyable experience for me.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>Author, Dreamweaver, Visionary</b>' is a fantastic choice to open the EP - with a captivating 40 seconds of prog-rock synth and guitar noodlings building up momentum to the crashing punk-rock drums and spiky alt-rock riffs that make up the bulk of the track. It's an energetic introduction to the band, with some fine instrumentation, but lacks the vocal hooks of the rest of the EP. '<b>All on Red</b>' is a mid-paced song, with softer guitar lines and a ballad-like vocal delivery. Although it may sound a little emo for some, it's the first time we are able to hear just how strong <b>Rich Bristow's</b> vocals are - his soulful delivery isn't common place for math-rock singers (who normally like to yelp - sometimes incomprehensibly).</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'<b>Welcome to Seaworld</b>' sounds the closest to what Foals produce - with a dancey drumbeat and layers of atmospheric guitar lines overshadowing a simple indie riff. Their most immediate song is '<b>Futures</b>', which contains a pop-punk sensibility built up around a massive chorus - very, very memorable. Closer '<b>Badminton</b>' contains the most irregular time-signature, with a math-drum line propelling inventive dual guitar-work and soaring vocal melodies - all backed by some understated violin and cello. Just when you think the song has drawn to a quiet conclusion, up jumps an up-tempo, <i>Biffy Clyro</i>-esque stabbing riff, in unison with stabbing strings. A thrilling end to the EP.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The reason I find <b>Likes Lions</b> so appealing is because they don't try to shove the irregularity of their riffs, beats and structures down your throat - like a lot of alternative math-rock bands (I think it makes them feel progressive). Instead, they use their experimental instrumentation as a unique backdrop to the kinds of pop-rock hooks that can stay with you for the rest of the day. Can't wait to see what they'll come up with next. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">For fans of <i>Tellison</i> (and, of course,<i> Foals</i>).  <a href="http://likeslions.bandcamp.com/"><b>Download 'Future Colour' EP</b></a> // <a href="http://www.facebook.com/likeslions"><b>Likes Lions</b></a></div>||
EP Review : FaltyDL - Atlantis|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-HyFkJnb8gY0/Tu9ES-M7-vI/AAAAAAAADNM/ij2lnk0QXTY/s1600/5021392691190.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-HyFkJnb8gY0/Tu9ES-M7-vI/AAAAAAAADNM/ij2lnk0QXTY/s320/5021392691190.jpg" width="320"/></a></div>Released earlier last month, '<b>Atlantis</b>' is the new EP from <b>FaltyDL</b>. Known to his friends as <b>Drew Lustman</b>, FaltyDL has steadily been making a name for himself stateside as '<i>one of the hottest names in electronic music</i>'. He has an impressive work rate, putting out two albums, an EP, and three singles all since 2008. Now the New York based artist is ready to release another in the shape of this four-track EP, which is his first record for <b>Ninja Tune</b>.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">'Atlantis' is an album which pays homage to Lustman's musical knowledge and history, as well as demonstrating his ears desire to take his sounds to a new level. The title track has an almost inaudibly low bass droning throughout as a rhythmic beat commands you to move. Whilst obvious comparisons can be drawn with <i>Fourtet</i> on the opening track, FaltyDL opens things up on '<b>Can't Stop The Prophet</b>', as the pace is slowed right down and a weird synth and strings combination proceeds to put you into a dream like state, before it all goes drum and bassy near the end. '<b>My Light, My Love</b>' carries on in similar vain, with chilled but off kilter beats seemingly lulling you into a strange vortex where you can't escape. Final track '<b>The Sale Ends</b>' is a more conventional minimal track, perfect for that 4am vibe. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Whilst his high productivity may lead to some questioning the continued quality of his work, FaltyDL shows that variation is the key here. This four track record shows that he has plenty of interesting ideas floating around his head, and to put a marker on that creativity would be disastrous for both him and us.<br/><br/><b>Atlantis</b> is out now through <a href="http://ninjatune.net/release/faltydl/atlantis-ep"><b>Ninja Tune</b></a> // <a href="http://faltydl.tumblr.com/"><b>FaltyDL</b></a></div>||
EP Review : Sea Oleena - Sleeplessness|<div style="text-align: justify;">Standing at seven tracks in length, <b>Sea Oleena’s</b> new release '<b>Sleeplessness</b>' could be considered more mini-album than EP, but that still wouldn’t justify the enormity of the music recorded by Montréal multi-instrumentalist<b> Charlotte Loseth</b>. The record is a beautiful warm blanket of songs, each one an epic cacophony of layered sounds, reverb and haunting female vocals delivered with the unassuming charm of a girl humming a song in her bedroom.<br/><br/>Each hushed swirl of a song bleeds into the next, joined together by the rumbling and eerie ambient sounds throughout. For what on first listen could be dismissed as the twee ramblings of yet another coy female artist, scratch the surface of Loseth’s musical landscape and it’s like walking into Narnia. There’s wonder at every turn.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Vocals sounding like mere ethereal whispers hide beautiful poetry: “<i>Invisible physicians, lawyers, and magicians / an instant of existence at the table in the kitchen</i>” she wails as the opening lines of this record. “<i>This is what he wrote in the ripped-up note: / I've become something even less than a ghost. / Even more of a though, I've become a mirage. / I'm the shaky air encircling the flickering flame. / I'm the white wall swallowing the window frame. hall</i>” she hisses over ‘<b>Insomnia Plague</b>’.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Instrumentation is orthodox but they’re whipped into yearning swirls of something more exquisite. Plucked acoustic guitars, pianos and echoy bass drums lay the foundations for Loseth’s, numerous but never overdone multiple vocal lines.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Perhaps if criticism could be levelled it’s that there are no standout tracks to be found on this record; no big choruses or sing along lyrics, just a body of delicate spacey folk that’s presented as a single entity. This of course is the point.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The magical world of Sleeplessness is intoxicating. It feels like Loseth creates such music for the purpose of sharing with the listener something greater than herself. This organic and ever shifting waterfall of a record demands and deserves our attention.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">All songs and lyrics are available on the <a href="http://seaoleena.bandcamp.com/album/sea-oleena"><b>Sea Oleena bandcamp</b></a> page, whilst the cassette version of this album (including her first self titled EP) can be purchased via <a href="http://www.bridgetownrecords.info/"><b>Bridgetown Records</b></a>. // <a href="http://seaoleena.bandcamp.com/"><b>Sea Oleena</b></a></div>||
EP Review : Alphabet Backwards - British Explorer|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-uDvFIweTIwE/Tud_wqL71kI/AAAAAAAADMw/tp7lXRk3pYo/s1600/1791726098-1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-uDvFIweTIwE/Tud_wqL71kI/AAAAAAAADMw/tp7lXRk3pYo/s320/1791726098-1.jpg" width="320"/></a></div>Recently released through <i>Highline Records</i>, '<b>British Explorer</b>' is a new three track EP from Oxford's <b>Alphabet Backwards</b>. With apparent support from the likes of <i>Huw Stephens</i>, <i>Tom Robinson</i>, and <i>Steve Lamacq</i>, the band have been making steady inroads during 2011, with their simple mission statement being to '<i>champion the noble art of pop music, dancing all the way</i>'. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Opening track '<b>Big Top</b>' brings up a clear comparison with Cardiff's <i>Los Campesinos!</i> with the dual combination of male and female vocals being a striking one, however some clever synths help to widen the gap between the bands' style, and Alphabet Backwards ear for a catchy melody is hard to ignore. '<b>Tonight</b>' carries on in a similar vein, with an interesting mix up of acoustic guitars put against the synths, as well as a clear appreciation of space within the song, which helps to broaden the bands' appeal. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The final track of this short record is '<b>Taller</b>', which is also the leading single to be taken from it. An obvious choice too after hearing the opening few bars, as some frankly irresistible vocals from frontman <i>James Hitchman</i> are played out over yet more guitar/synth based pop music. I think what helps make <b>Alphabet Backwards</b> stand out over their pop loving piers is that they do keep things simple, not being afraid to let their music and lyrics stand up for themselves, as opposed to other acts who throw everything into it hoping something will stick.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The 'British Explorer' EP is <a href="http://alphabackwards.bandcamp.com/"><b>available now</b></a> through <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Highline-Records/161884757209312"><b>Highline Records</b></a> // <a href="http://www.alphabetbackwards.net/"><b>Alphabet Backwards</b></a></div>||
EP Review : Daughter - The Wild Youth|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Jc2FxsxQDSI/TuIXd1gD-WI/AAAAAAAADMo/DRmsvcgAqVE/s1600/509061585-1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Jc2FxsxQDSI/TuIXd1gD-WI/AAAAAAAADMo/DRmsvcgAqVE/s320/509061585-1.jpg" width="320"/></a></div><b>Daughter</b> are <i>Elena Tonra</i> and <i>Igor Haefeli</i>, a double act that have swept through 2011 with numerous gigs across the UK, put out an EP titled '<b>His Young Heart</b>', and they end the year with another record, '<b>The Wild Youth</b>', which is out through <b>Communion Records</b>.<br/><br/>Personally I first discovered Daughter whilst they were supporting <i>Benjamin Francis Leftwich</i> during his Autumn tour, catching their intimate and spell-bounding show at the Union Chapel in Islington, where their exquisite performance equalled if not better that of the headliner.<br/><br/>'<b>The Wild Youth</b>' begins with '<b>Home</b>', a track which showcases what makes Daughter so utterly brilliant. Elena and Igor have an ear to create space within their music, moments where their instruments can breath and the listener can fully appreciate the beauty that is being played out before them. The poignant combination of Elena's lingering vocals and the delicate acoustic/electric guitars demonstrate how simplicity in music is something to be applauded.<br/><br/>'<b>Medicine</b>' is built upon simple piano chords, with the focus put upon the beautiful words and vocals, as is '<b>Love</b>', with Elena's mystical vocals driving the song along as drums and guitars slowly build to a gentle crescendo. My favourite track on the record is '<b>Youth</b>', with the thought provoking lyrics having the perfect backdrop of drawn-out music to stand out and be counted.<br/><br/>It's testament to Daughter's belief and confidence in their own ideas that they give their music almost a license to bask and shine in its simplicity, and how grateful we must be for that. Music Liberation eagerly awaits a full length release in 2012...<br/><br/><a href="http://ohdaughter.bandcamp.com/album/the-wild-youth-ep"><b>You can buy 'The Wild Youth' EP now</b></a> // <a href="http://www.facebook.com/ohdaughter"><b>Daughter</b></a> // <a href="http://www.communionmusic.co.uk/"><b>Communion Records</b></a> </div>||
New Video : Gabrielle Aplin - Home|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-_A3lDOVzQ6U/Tt-UaB4OLHI/AAAAAAAADMY/1O2Xu74tf5Y/s1600/206591_10150148314976026_142481721025_6766777_364025_n.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="214" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-_A3lDOVzQ6U/Tt-UaB4OLHI/AAAAAAAADMY/1O2Xu74tf5Y/s320/206591_10150148314976026_142481721025_6766777_364025_n.jpg" width="320"/></a></div>We first caught up with <b>Gabrielle Aplin</b> back in August 2010, when we carried out a <a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2010/08/interview-gabrielle-aplin.html"><b>quick-fire interview</b></a> with her, learning lots of interesting things like discovering her favourite sandwich is "<i>Brie, Grape, and Cranberry</i>". Since that momentous occasion she has released a couple of EPs alongside some constant touring up and down the UK, as well as playing at this years Glastonbury Festival. 2012 see's the release of her third EP titled '<b>Home</b>' through <b>Never Fade Records</b>, of which the title track we have the video for.<br/><br/>It's a beautiful song, showcasing Gabrielle's delicate and ethereal voice, as well as a songwriting ability beyond her tender years. The video is also quite special, directed by <a href="http://www.youtube.com/redirect?q=http%3A%2F%2Fjoshuasanger.co.uk%2F&amp;session_token=EjxPG90ENpCg3qzju-DDj2Fh2EZ8MTMyMzM1OTEwM0AxMzIzMjcyNzAz"><b>Joshua Sanger</b></a> it features some stunning shots of Gabrielle and the English countryside.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">You can <a href="http://itunes.apple.com/gb/preorder/home-ep/id484072513"><b>pre-order</b></a> '<b>Home</b>' ahead of the January 9th release date. // <a href="http://gabrielleaplin.co.uk/"><b>Gabrielle Aplin</b></a></div>||
The Blog Sound of 2012|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-WWFoDdRabm0/TtqUGurMR7I/AAAAAAAADMQ/PHnB0llDtxg/s1600/The-Blog-Sound-2012.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="240" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-WWFoDdRabm0/TtqUGurMR7I/AAAAAAAADMQ/PHnB0llDtxg/s320/The-Blog-Sound-2012.jpg" width="320"/></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;">As some of you may or may not know, the BBC have a yearly 'Sound Of ...' list, whereby they feature a longlist of 15 artists they think will have a successful year ahead. This initial longlist gets whittled down to a top 5, with eventually an overall winner being chosen. <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/music/soundof/2011/"><b>2011</b></a> saw <i>Jessie J</i> being picked, <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/music/soundof/2010/"><b>2010</b></a> was <i>Ellie Goulding</i>, <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/music/soundof/2009/"><b>2009</b></a> was <i>Little Boots</i>, and so on. The lists are compiled by a team of 'experts', ranging from music critics, editors, broadcasters, and bloggers.</div></div><div style="text-align: justify;">As some of you may or may not know, the BBC have a yearly 'Sound Of ...' list, whereby they feature a longlist of 15 artists they think will have a successful year ahead. This initial longlist gets whittled down to a top 5, with eventually an overall winner being chosen. <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/music/soundof/2011/"><b>2011</b></a> saw <i>Jessie J</i> being picked, <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/music/soundof/2010/"><b>2010</b></a> was <i>Ellie Goulding</i>, <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/music/soundof/2009/"><b>2009</b></a> was <i>Little Boots</i>, and so on. The lists are compiled by a team of 'experts', ranging from music critics, editors, broadcasters, and bloggers.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Well in an attempt to try something a bit different, three of the most esteemed bloggers out there (Andy VonPip from <a href="http://vonpipmusicalexpress.wordpress.com/"><b>The Von Pip Musical Express</b></a>, Robin from <a href="http://breakingmorewaves.blogspot.com/"><b>Breaking More Waves</b></a>, and Simon from <a href="http://sweepingthenation.blogspot.com/"><b>Sweeping The Nation</b></a>) decided it would be an interesting experiment to run a similar type of poll, with the votes coming solely from music bloggers. They say:-</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">"<i>We mooted the idea of conducting a poll of the UK’s best music blogs &amp; asking them who they thought would be the “Sound Of 2012.” We hoped by having an ‘alternative’ it may throw up some interesting results which we could  contrast and compare  to the Beebs ‘official’ one .  It was felt that an alternative music “Bloggers Sound of ...” list could highlight what’s really been going on musically, down at the coalface so to speak.</i>"<br/><br/>So without further ado here are the top 15 artists that us music bloggers chose! (Music Liberation's choices will be revealed in early January!)<br/><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><a href="http://www.houdinidax.co.uk/"><b>Houdini Dax</b></a><b> / </b><a href="http://www.myspace.com/liannelahavas"><b>Lianne De Haves</b></a><b> / </b><a href="http://www.themeparkband.com/"><b>Theme Park</b></a><b> / </b><a href="http://frenchwives.co.uk/"><b>French Wives</b></a><b> / <a href="http://www.thegoodnatured.co.uk/">The Good Natured</a> / </b><a href="http://www.facebook.com/altJ.band"><b>Alt J</b></a><b> / </b><a
