Cutting Noise Podcast 002 (November 2011)|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"></div><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-9-jw4uc453Y/TtecrRmXtsI/AAAAAAAADL0/Kh4y9dnIP5k/s1600/cuttingnoisesimple_reasonably_small.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-9-jw4uc453Y/TtecrRmXtsI/AAAAAAAADL0/Kh4y9dnIP5k/s1600/cuttingnoisesimple_reasonably_small.jpg"/></a>The new <b>Cutting Noise</b> podcast is now available to stream and download. Running in association with <b>Music Liberation</b> the monthly podcasts aim to deliver 10 new tracks discovered during the past month.<br/><br/>You can follow Cutting Noise on <a href="http://www.twitter.com/cutting_noise"><b>twitter</b></a>, <a href="http://www.facebook.com/cuttingnoise"><b>facebook</b></a>, and <a href="http://cuttingnoise.tumblr.com/"><b>tumblr</b></a>.<br/><br/>As well as listening to all the previous podcasts on <a href="http://soundcloud.com/cuttingnoise"><b>soundcloud</b></a>.</div>||
Album Review : Hectic Zeniths - Hectic Zeniths|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-sdBq5rHEplQ/TtUyP324sEI/AAAAAAAADLc/DV2uRtc_PS4/s1600/2243870907-1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-sdBq5rHEplQ/TtUyP324sEI/AAAAAAAADLc/DV2uRtc_PS4/s320/2243870907-1.jpg" width="320"/></a></div><b>Hectic Zeniths’</b> self titled debut is the work of Brooklyn, NY native and current Philadelphia resident <b>Adam Morgan Prince</b>. His moniker is an anagram of <i>Zeitschtichen</i>, a German word meaning shifts in, or layers of time. This is an apt name for both the artist and the album, as each track is a richly layered, brooding soundscape.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Anyone who frequents <a href="http://qn5.com/discuss/"><i>QN5 Music’s forum</i></a> will already be aware of what happens when Prince gets hold of a piano. Under the moniker ‘<i>amplifya</i>’, his take on <i>CunninLynguists</i>’ ‘<a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KHwDG_fnY"><b><i>The Light</i></b></a>’ from the <i>QN5 Rmx Vol. 2 EP</i> (2006) was well received, whilst he also showcased his chops in a cover of ‘<a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AJao0YQjEIE&amp;feature=player_embedded"><b><i>Gathered</i></b></a>’ from <i>Tonedeff’s Archetype</i> (2005).</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">His album follows a loose formula and is successful for it. Most of the tracks are built around a melancholy piano section and either live or sampled drums. Added to this are vocal samples that work like added instrumentation, violins and a couple of tracks featuring guitar (‘<b>Why Shoot Debris About It</b>’ and ‘<b>Zeitschtichen</b>’), making a dark and sombre LP that is perfect for bumping in your headphones on a cold winter morning.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The intro, ‘<b>One That Got Away</b>’ sets the mood well, with reversed strings, a mournful vocal sample and playful beat, before segueing into the first piano led track, ‘<b>Then and Now</b>’. The album goes from strength to strength from there. ‘<b>I Might Drown</b>’, a standout among an album full of strong cuts, features an upbeat drum pattern that contrasts the subtle keys, haunting vocals that drift eerily in and out of the song and the dramatic bursts of violin. The subtle guitar in ‘<b>Zeitschtichen</b>’ compliments the piano and plodding beat well and an airy vocal weaving through the piece wraps things up nicely.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">While never reaching their cinematic heights, <b>Hectic Zeniths</b> draws comparisons with <i>Blue Sky Black Death</i> or <i>Emancipator</i>, each known for creating rich and densely layered music. At eleven tracks long and clocking in at half an hour from beginning to end, some may feel it may be on the short side, but with each song containing so many elements, replay value will undoubtedly be high.<br/><br/>Hectic Zeniths will be released 10th January 2012, you can<b> </b><a href="http://hecticzeniths.bandcamp.com/"><b>stream or pre-order the album now</b></a><br/></div>||
New Music : Rosa Valle / Therapist / Smother Party|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div style="text-align: justify;"><b><u>Rosa Valle</u></b></div><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><b><u>Rosa Valle</u></b></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Uncompromising math rock four-piece from Middlesborough, <b>Rosa Valle</b> recently released their debut EP titled '<b>Holy Bermuda</b>', through a split between <b>Holy Roar Records</b> and <b>Big Scary Monsters</b>. Sounding like a cross between Rolo<i> Tomassi</i> at their heaviest, <i>Foals</i> at their gentlest, and <i>The Murder of Rosa Luxemburg</i> at their craziest, this EP demonstrates a band with a clear belief in their ideas and a band who possess an inherent desire to express themselves in whatever way they see fit. I'm expecting big things from these chaps when it comes to the recording of their debut LP. *Recommended track - '<b>Mathemagician</b>'.*</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Stream the record on <a href="http://rosavalle.bandcamp.com/"><b>bandcamp</b></a>.  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/rosavallemusic"><b>Rosa Valle</b></a>  <a href="http://holyroarrecords.com/"><b>Holy Roar Records</b></a>  <a href="http://www.bsmrocks.com/"><b>Big Scary Monsters</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Bursting out of Phoenix CA come <b>Therapist</b>, a bouncy electro punk act who first came to our attention with the track '<b>I Know What I Want</b>'. Released through <b>Indian Gold Records</b>, that song was very much reminiscent of the likes of  <i>Teenagersintokyo</i>, <i>Chaingang</i>, and <i>Operator Please</i>, with the stop start jerky combo of the vocals and the bands stripped back electro punk working to great effect. This week the band releases their debut EP, titled '<b>Hearts Beats</b>', featuring more of the same bass heavy electro punk vibes. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Grab a <a href="http://wearetherapist.bandcamp.com/"><b>download/stream</b></a> now.  <a href="http://wearetherapist.blogspot.com/"><b>Therapist</b></a>  <a href="http://indiangoldrecords.blogspot.com/"><b>Indian Gold Records</b></a></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><u><b>Smother Party</b></u></div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Based out of Brooklyn, <b>Smother Party</b> are a groove laden instrumental rock three-piece who earlier this year released their debut album, '<b>Casa Limon</b>'. Whilst being a challenging album it will reward those who stick with it, as repeated plays open up a whole new world of what can be acheived with two guitars and a drum kit. In parts bewildering, in parts brilliant, 'Casa Limon' showcases a band with abstract ideas above the 'normal' rockers station. Particularly of note is the sound of the guitars on this album, which almost sound out of tune at times but are still somehow hugely rhythmic and head nod-able, like '<a href="http://smotherparty.bandcamp.com/track/serious-beef"><b>Serious Beef</b></a>'.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Stream/Download on <a href="http://smotherparty.bandcamp.com/"><b>bandcamp</b></a>  <a href="http://variantrecords.com/index.html"><b>Variant Records</b></a>  <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Smother-Party/106362182748082?sk=wall"><b>Smother Party</b></a></div>||
New Video : The Producers - Episode 2: The Bullitts|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-6owaOV0wenc/Tsw4R2kBiDI/AAAAAAAADK8/f2F7qtOF-bg/s1600/The+Bullits19.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" height="213" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-6owaOV0wenc/Tsw4R2kBiDI/AAAAAAAADK8/f2F7qtOF-bg/s320/The+Bullits19.jpg" width="320"/></a></div>We featured <b>The Bullitts</b> earlier this year with a single review of '<a href="http://musicliberation.blogspot.com/2011/08/single-review-bullitts-jay-electronica.html"><b>Run &amp; Hide</b></a>', a collaborative track that featured <b>Jay Electronica</b>. We also enthused about the '<i>beautifully crafted cinematic experience</i>' that accompanied the song, a pattern which has been repeated with each track that has been taken from The Bullitts debut LP '<b>They'll Die By Dawn And Other Short Stories</b>'. Well now thanks to a new six part music documentary being put together by <a href="http://www.redbullstudios.com/"><b><i>Red Bull Studios</i></b></a> and <a href="http://www.vice.com/en_uk"><b><i>Vice Media</i></b></a> titled '<a href="http://www.vice.com/the-producers"><b>The Producers</b></a>', you can now meet the man behind <a href="http://www.facebook.com/thebullitts"><b>The Bullitts</b></a>, the enthralling <b>Jeymes Samuel</b>. </div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">In episode 2 of the ongoing series, Jeymes talks about everything connected with his love for music and films, as well as behind the scenes footage of him working with <i>Syience</i> on a short film project score. It's really quite inspiring stuff, and shows a man with a genuine interest for making art, with a clear intent on truly making a mark on those around him.</div>||
Album Review : Evidence - Cats & Dogs|<div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-TDn-5iXqrF0/TsqJrVtvrJI/AAAAAAAADKk/SeI1dQ78h4o/s1600/Evidence-Cats-Dogs-Artwork.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-TDn-5iXqrF0/TsqJrVtvrJI/AAAAAAAADKk/SeI1dQ78h4o/s320/Evidence-Cats-Dogs-Artwork.jpg" width="320"/></a></div>As is often the case with artists that earn critical acclaim, ‘backpackers’ favourite, LA’s <a href="http://www.dilatedpeoples.com/"><b>Dilated Peoples</b></a> never seemed to be able to turn that praise into the commercial success they deserve. With four albums under their belts, <b>DJ Babu</b>, <b>Rakaa Iriscience</b> and <b>Evidence</b> decided to take a break from recording as a group and focus on their solo careers. Of the group’s two lyricists, it is <b>Evidence</b> that has successfully managed to maintain something of a cult following in an increasingly crowded hip hop market.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">Following the meteorology theme Ev started on his well-received debut LP<b> 'The Weatherman</b>' in 2007, <b>Cats &amp; Dogs</b> is his first release for Minneapolis based <b>Rhymesayers Entertainment</b>.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">While Evidence may not be the most technically gifted emcee, his voice is engaging, his flow polished and on every track he oozes a laidback confidence that fans of West Coast Hip Hop will be familiar with.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">What does need to highlighted, though, is Ev’s ear for beats. Simply put, it is impeccable. While he is himself an accomplished producer, only two tracks on the album ('<b>I Don’t Need Love</b>' and '<b>Late For The Sky</b>') boast his name in the liner notes, even then only with co-production credits. Instead he hands production duties to long-time friend and collaborator <b>The Alchemist</b>, duo <b>Sid Roams</b>, <b>Rahki</b>, <b>Charli Brown</b> and <b>Twiz the Beat King</b>, the lesser-known names more than holding their own in esteemed company as the album shifts from soulful and introspective to big and brash seamlessly.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-mwCBQUF7HHk/TsqJ8ud5cTI/AAAAAAAADKs/99Tjn5a5CBs/s1600/evidence-300x225.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: right; float: right; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: 1em;"><img border="0" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-mwCBQUF7HHk/TsqJ8ud5cTI/AAAAAAAADKs/99Tjn5a5CBs/s1600/evidence-300x225.jpg"/></a></div><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The album also features the legendary <b>DJ Premier</b> who laces the understated single '<i><b>You</b></i>' and the darker, horn-based album closer '<i><b>Epilogue</b></i>' with his trademark chopped samples and scratched hooks, to the delight of this fan-boy, at least.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">The featured guests are also strong. <b>Aloe Blacc</b> drops in to add some soul to the sinister opener '<b><i>The Liner Notes</i>'</b> and '<i><b>The Red Carpet</b></i>' sees Evidence hold his own with two of Rap’s most celebrated lyricists; <b>Raekwon</b> (of <i>Wu-Tang Clan</i>) and West Coast veteran, <b>Ras Kass</b> over a smooth vocal-sample based Alchemist backdrop. Label mates <b>Slug</b> and <b>Aesop Rock</b> turn up on Emo-Rap fans’ wet-dream '<i><b>Late To The Sky</b></i>' and underground Rap’s current golden boy (and deservedly so) <b>Roc Marciano</b> blesses the moody strings and guitar lick of '<b>Fame</b>' alongside Mobb Deep’s Prodigy.</div><div style="text-align: justify;"><br/></div><div style="text-align: justify;">With no trace of a radio-friendly single or a floor-filling club banger, <b>Cats &amp; Dogs</b> may not win <b>Evidence</b> new fans, but after two decades in the business, it is clear that isn’t important to him. He knows his strengths and he plays to them.<br/><br/>If you like whiplash-inducing beats and solid rhymes, you won’t go wrong with this LP.<br/><br/>You can buy the album now from <a href="http://rhymesayers.com/"><b>Rhymesayers Entertainment</b></a> // <a href="https://www.facebook.com/misterevidence"><b>Evidence</b></a><br/><br/><b>[*</b>Many thanks to <b>Tom Nash</b> for his first article for <b>Music Liberation</b>, find out more about Tom on his <a href="http://blog.thewritetomnash.co.uk/"><b>The Write Tom Nash</b></a> site.<b>*]</b></div>||
